Japanese Obtain Land Rights in Harbin 83

Long-Standing Case Resolved at Once

Eastern Special Party Authorities Flatter Japan and Relinquish Rights

Harbin Correspondence: The issue of real estate registration in the Special Zone has been a long-standing dispute between China and Japan. At the end of November last year, a certain newspaper in Harbin suddenly claimed that the Eastern Special land lease issue, which had been in dispute for nine years, had now come to an end. On the Chinese side, the Director of the Land Administration Bureau made a statement saying that the land issue had been resolved several years ago, and that the Japanese registration was actually an acceptance of China's claim. On the Japanese side, however, they claimed that the issue had only recently been resolved and was beneficial to foreigners, and that from now on, the Japanese could ensure their ownership of land in the Shitoudao Street area of Harbin and seek development along the Eastern Railway line. Outsiders naturally find it difficult to understand the truth of the matter. However, the Japanese have always disregarded the regulations promulgated by the Chinese authorities. Now, after the Northeast has been occupied, they suddenly eagerly change contracts. The reason for this is not difficult to imagine. Now, please allow me to describe the process of how this issue arose.

The Eastern Provinces Special Zone, formerly the Eastern Railway’s affiliated land, was initially formed when the Eastern Railway was built. Land along the railway line was occupied without compensation or purchased from the people at low prices, covering a very wide area. Thus, a railway-affiliated land was formed that was somewhat similar to a leased territory. Later, after the Changda Line south of Changchun was transferred to Japan, there were still 10,550 remaining, which equals 18,761.78 acres. The annual land revenue is about one million rubles. This type of land, formed within China, created all sorts of abnormal situations. After the overthrow of the Tsarist Russian government, our country recovered administrative power along the Eastern Railway line and established the Eastern Provinces Special Zone. It was necessary to recover these land rights. In July of the 12th year of the Republic of China (1923), the former Director of the Special Zone, Zhu Qinglan, together with the Garrison Commander of Binjiang, Zhang Huanxiang, formulated measures to take over the Eastern Railway Land Management Office, which were implemented on August 1st. The takeover was completed, and the Eastern Provinces Special Zone Land Administration Bureau was established the following day to inherit the tasks of the Eastern Railway Land Management Office.

However, the consulates of the countries in Harbin at the time were greatly dissatisfied with China's recovery of rights and filed protests one after another. As a result, the Eastern Railway Land Management Office was allowed to continue to exist, but its authority was reduced. At the same time, the Sino-Russian Conference opened in Beijing. The Russians expressed concessions on the land issue, so the influence of the Land Administration Bureau gradually increased. When the Sino-Russian Fengtian Agreement was concluded, the Chinese Eastern Railway became a purely commercial organization with no land rights outside the railway line. The Eastern Railway Land Management Office was thus effectively eliminated, and the Land Administration Bureau had full power over the land along the Eastern Railway line.

However, the Eight Stations issue occurred at the end of the 13th year of the Republic of China (1924). At that time, the Russian Director of the Eastern Railway, Ivanov, believed that the Eight Stations were necessary land for the Eastern Railway's operation and began to collect taxes in the area. The Chinese side, however, believed that the Russians had clearly given up their land rights in the Sino-Russian Fengtian Agreement and could not recognize this matter. The public also held fierce demonstrations to urge the government. As a result, on January 1, 1925, the Chinese government announced real estate regulations in the Special Zone, stating that any contract not registered with the local court would have no legal effect. This led to protests from foreign consuls, claiming that this regulation hindered the rights of foreigners not subject to Chinese jurisdiction. The Japanese side advocated this even more strongly. At that time, the Japanese Consul-General, Ayasuke Eiji, tried various methods to abolish this registration measure. The Chinese side, on the one hand, replied to the other side, stating that real estate registration was not a litigation matter and had nothing to do with consular jurisdiction. On the other hand, the Director of the Land Administration Bureau, Zhang Huanxiang, issued Proclamation No. 50 on December 15, 1926, and Proclamation No. 51 on December 20 of the same month to show that the matter was inevitable.

The main points of these two proclamations were roughly to abolish the old Russian contracts and register again, issuing Chinese contracts. If these procedures were not followed, all transfers and name changes would be invalid. Ten articles of simplified rental regulations were also formulated, stipulating that property owners must fulfill the following obligations: (1) Abide by Chinese laws and local regulations; (2) The purpose of investment is limited to self-use and businesses operated by oneself; (3) Pay municipal taxes and not intentionally delay payment.

These regulations are the most lenient among the methods used by any country in the world to treat foreign residents. However, the Japanese and other foreign consuls still believed that they harmed their treaty interests and insisted on overturning them. Because there was no hope of resolution in Harbin, they notified their residents not to pay taxes and not to register, while the diplomatic corps in Beijing negotiated with the Zhang Zuolin government. (At that time, Zhang formed the Grand Marshal's Office in Beijing, and after Zhang's failure to leave the pass and the Huanggutun Incident, it was transferred back to local management.) In September 1928, the Japanese Consul-General in Harbin even used the saying "no taxation without representation" as a condition for Japanese residents to pay municipal taxes, and negotiated with our country to elect a committee to the municipal council as a prerequisite, thus intruding into the political sphere. The Japanese have completely achieved their goals in this section, but the land issue has not yet been resolved. When the outgoing Japanese Consul in Harbin, Yagi Motohachi, left office, he still considered this to be his greatest regret.

After the arrival of the new Japanese Consul, Ohashi Chuichi, the consuls of other countries no longer mentioned this land issue, but the Japanese Consul continued to work hard. After the September 18th Incident occurred last year, according to Japanese newspapers, he made the following remarks to the Japanese, announcing the results of the land issue: (1) The real estate registration regulations of the Eastern Provinces Special Zone of January 1925 do not apply to Japanese people. The transfer contract of real estate held by Japanese people does not need to go through the court and can be declared at the Land Administration Bureau. (2) Abolish Proclamation No. 50 and Proclamation No. 51 of December 1926. Japanese people only need to undergo a slight qualification review by the Chinese side to retain old properties and accept new properties. (3) Japan has de facto recognition of the Land Administration Bureau, which it has not recognized in the past.

These declarations are very inconsistent with what the Chinese side has claimed. The actual facts cannot be known, but the Japanese side congratulated each other, celebrating the solidification of property rights in the Shitoudao Street industry in Harbin. The Japanese have a lot of real estate in Shitoudao Street (the Toyo Colonization Company alone has more than 1,000 tsubo, which is about 34,000 square feet in Chinese measurements.)

According to Japanese newspapers, as of December 28, 1931, there were 31 cases of Japanese people's Russian land deeds being exchanged for Chinese land deeds in the Land Administration Bureau. The distribution of owners is as follows: Toyo Colonization Company 19 cases, North Huic Electric Company 1 case, Land Construction Company 1 case, Far East Transportation Company 1 case, Eastern Provinces Industrial Company 1 case, Mitsui & Co. 1 case, Harbin Bank 1 case, Kiue Store 1 case, Yokohama Specie Bank 3 cases, North Manchurian Development Company 2 cases, totaling 31 cases. (The Toyo Colonization Company actually has a lot of land in Korea and the three northeastern provinces.) It is heard that the South Manchuria Railway Company also plans to build a grand building on Shitoudao Street as a central organization for the Japanese. It will have four floors. The underground floor will be a large club composed of a dance hall, ice skating rink, indoor sports field, dining hall, and bar. The ground floor and the second floor will be shops and banks, and the third and fourth floors will be residences. If these buildings become a reality, they will greatly prosper Shitoudao Street. What we must pay attention to is that after the Japanese have obtained land rights, the various countries of France, England, America, and Italy will inevitably demand the same, and the land ownership in Harbin will fall into the hands of foreigners, and the danger is enormous. (January 15)

Guangdong Army Recovers Xinfeng on the Jiangxi Border 84

Peng Dehuai's Forces Have Collapsed and Retreated

Ganzhou City Has Not Fallen

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Jiangxi communist bandits, taking advantage of the recent political instability and urgent foreign troubles, are attempting to make a show of force. The Zhu De and Mao Zedong divisions are engaging in large-scale activities, and the entire eastern and southern Jiangxi provinces have been ravaged. At the same time, the Guangdong province border defense has become strained. The Guangdong authorities have specially dispatched Li Yangjing's Third Army to Zhenzhe in eastern Jiangxi. The original troops in Dongjiang were the Second Army, Zhang Meixin's First Division, and the First and Second Independent Brigades. The newly added Third Army has two divisions, totaling five divisions and three independent regiments, which should be sufficient to deploy in the Chaozhou-Meizhou border area. After the Third Army was withdrawn to Beijiang, all Beijiang defense was entirely deployed by the First Army, Yu Hanmou's troops. The Second Division, Ye Zhao's troops, are stationed in the area of Shixing, Nanxiong, and Zhoutian. The First Division, Li Zhenqiu's troops, are stationed in the area of Shaoguan, Lechang, Yingde, and Wengyuan. Army Commander Yu Hanmou personally went to the front on the 19th to inspect the Beijiang defense. Xinfeng, above Nanxiong, is currently guarded by the First Independent Brigade, Fan Dexing's troops, and jointly defended with the Jiangxi Army, Ma Kun's Brigade, in Ganzhou. The recent Shanghai newspaper report that Ganzhou was captured by bandits on the 3rd of this month is a misrepresentation. We have received a telegram from Ma Kun proving it is inaccurate. However, Xinfeng City in southern Jiangxi did indeed fall once. The county was originally garrisoned by the Second Regiment, Liao Daoming's troops, dispatched by Fan Dexing's Brigade of the Guangdong Army. Later, due to the intensifying bandit forces, the regiment moved to the Dageng border, 30 miles outside Xinfeng City, for the convenience of communication. Xinfeng County was temporarily defended by more than 700 militiamen. Recently, the communist bandit Peng Dehuai's forces discovered that the city was empty and suddenly led more than 1,000 bandits to besiege Xinfeng County on the 13th of this month. The militiamen in the city were unable to resist and lost the city in the evening. On the 14th, Fan's Brigade heard the news and dispatched Liao Daoming's Regiment again to attack fiercely, and also dispatched a machine gun company to assist in the attack. They fought fiercely with the bandits for two days and nights. The communist bandits ran out of ammunition and abandoned the city and fled on the 16th. Liao's Regiment entered the city that morning to handle the aftermath. On the 17th, they reported the details of the recapture of Xinfeng to the Commander-in-Chief of the First Group Army. (January 19)

Hubei Province Begins to Ban Opium 85

Hankou Correspondence: Hubei Province has been brewing an opium ban for a long time, and now a Opium Prohibition Committee has been established to be responsible for handling it. On the 22nd, the committee appointed special investigators for each county and city, and announced that it would be implemented from today. The proclamation stated that the harm of opium is worse than floods and beasts, and the central government has issued clear orders to ban it. However, because the Hubei and Hunan regions are close to Sichuan and Guizhou, there is an excessive amount of stockpiled goods. The procurement of these goods was before the opium ban, and the funds involved are of great financial importance to the region. Merchants petitioned the former Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force for approval to sell off old goods within a limited time to alleviate the merchants' difficulties, and an office was set up to supervise the cleaning up in order to eliminate them as soon as possible. Except for the

Page 11

Continued Important News 86

transport and sale, which is responsible for the cleanup by the Hubei Special Tax Office, all prohibited planting and smoking should set up special management agencies, hoping to receive the effect of division of labor and cooperation. Now, the committee has been established in accordance with the order of the Hubei Provincial Government, and has still formulated various rules for the opium ban in accordance with the Opium Prohibition Law and submitted them to the Hubei Provincial Government for deliberation and approval. The methods are: (1) Absolutely prohibit the planting of opium seedlings to eliminate the roots. (2) Absolutely prohibit the smuggling, transport, and sale of drugs such as morphine, red and white pills, Gaogen, and heroin, in order to eliminate the root of the poison. (3) Absolutely prohibit young men and women from smoking. (4) All opium smokers should register with the opium prohibition agencies in each county and city in accordance with the regulations, and request the issuance of opium cessation licenses to quit smoking in stages. The opium cessation medicine should be purchased from licensed stores for verification. Those without a license are not allowed to purchase and smoke, and violators will be punished as contraband. (5) Places similar to opium dens that provide smoking are places that hide dirt and harbor criminals and have special chapters to strictly ban them. Those that have been established should immediately apply for registration, and only be allowed to reduce the number of places, not increase. (6) During the cleanup period, only licensed stores that have paid special taxes are allowed to sell opium cessation medicine. If there is private smuggling or smoking, once discovered, they will be punished according to the regulations. If people report and are arrested as a result, 40% of the fine will be used as a reward, 30% will be used as a bonus for cooperating personnel, and the remaining 30% will be submitted to the committee as opium prohibition funds. Opium is rampant throughout Hubei Province. The authorities have been taking a laissez-faire attitude in order to greedily collect taxes. Now that a special opium prohibition agency has been established, it seems that it will change to intervention from now on. (January 22)

Chen Diaoyuan Sends Personnel to Wuhu to Raise Funds 87

Planning to Borrow 300,000 Yuan from Salt Merchants

And Also Dispatching 200,000 Yuan in Road Construction Bonds

Wuhu Correspondence: The Anhui Provincial Government owes at least 700,000 yuan in various party and government expenses for the past year. The income from land taxes and miscellaneous taxes in various counties has been almost cut off due to the impact of the floods. The salt surtax and collaborative funds promised by the central government (about 270,000 yuan per month) have not been allocated for both December of last year and January of this year. The expenses for Chen Diaoyuan's 46th Division, Yue Shengxuan's troops, the 55th Division, Ruan Zhaochang's troops, the 57th Division, Li Songshan's troops, and the garrison brigade (about 400,000 yuan per month) have also not been issued for two months. The need for funds is as urgent as fire. Liu Yumin, the director of the Finance Department, went to Beijing last time to demand the 500,000 yuan owed by the central government, but because no one was responsible in the Ministry of Finance, there were no results at all. He is still staying in Beijing. In view of this, Chen Diaoyuan specially sent Zuo Zonglian, the second section chief of the Finance Department, to Wuhu yesterday to contact the Salt Transportation Bureau, the Salt Affairs Inspection Office, and the salt merchants to borrow 300,000 yuan using the surtax that should be allocated by the central government as collateral. He also dispatched 200,000 yuan in road construction bonds to salt ticket merchants and water vendors, with a deadline for payment to the treasury in order to meet the urgent needs. After Zuo arrived in Wuhu, he contacted all parties, but there were no concrete results. Because the silver market in Wuhu is extremely tight, it is difficult to raise funds. Even if there is a solution, it will take a considerable amount of time. It is heard that after Zuo finishes his business in Wuhu, he will also go to Bengbu to discuss borrowing funds with the salt merchants in northern Anhui. (January 21)

Complete Resolution of the Fengxian Incident 88

Telegrams from Various Groups Reinstating the Reputation of Commander Zhang

All Detained Personnel Also Released by Commander Zhang

Xuzhou dispatch: Following an investigation into the Fengxian Incident by personnel dispatched by the Provincial Party Headquarters, the Provincial Government, and the Pacification Commissioner’s Office, as well as mediation by local gentry and Li Jiuling, a friend of Zhang Zhankui, groups in Fengxian telegraphed to reinstate the military reputation of the First Cavalry Division and undertook to provide supplies in accordance with provincial orders. Commander Zhang then released the detained personnel and returned the confiscated weapons. This mediation plan has now been implemented. The detained party committee member Dong Yujue, supervisory committee member Huang Tirun, battalion commander Zhu Dundian, and others have been released. The telegram issued by the Fengxian groups stated: "To the public across the nation: Having read recent reports in domestic newspapers alleging a mutiny and looting by the garrisoned Cavalry Division in Fengxian, as well as robberies of the Farmers' and Workers' Bank, shops, and residents, these are not the facts. The Third Cavalry Division has been stationed in Fengxian for several months, maintaining strict discipline, and enjoying harmonious relations with the local population. This incident originated from supply issues, which were exploited by malicious individuals to sow discord. The resulting misunderstanding was brewing for some time. The various rumors circulating outside are largely inaccurate. Both sides have now reached a mutual understanding, and past grievances have been completely resolved. All detained individuals have been released one after another, shaking hands and making amends as before. Furthermore, following this incident, personnel dispatched by high-level party and government agencies have thoroughly investigated the truth, which is now clear. All rumors have been dispelled. All agencies are now operating as usual, and the military and civilians are living in peace as before. In addition to reporting these circumstances to the Ministry of Military Affairs, the Provincial Government, and the Jiangsu Pacification Commissioner and Superintendent, we specially telegraph this to inform the public across the nation. Respectfully submitted by all agencies and legal groups in Fengxian." With the dispatch of this telegram, the Fengxian Incident has now come to an end. (22nd)

Local News

Songjiang 89

Motorized Rowing Boat Violently Collides with Hantong Bridge: The Hantong Bridge in Yexie Town, 14th District, is a cement and steel bridge. Yesterday (the 22nd) at approximately 2:00 PM, a Xin Feng boat (a rowing boat equipped with a motor) was traveling from Songjiang to Nanqiao, passing the eastern pier of the bridge. The boat owner, A Mao, accelerated the motor and collided violently with the bridge. With a loud crash, the entire bridge shook, causing pedestrians on the bridge to scatter in fear. Fortunately, the bridge did not collapse, but the incident caused temporary disorder among the local residents. Officer Xuan Jinquan from the local police station detained the boat and the boat owner, A Mao, who will be sent to Songjiang today for further investigation. The district chief, Gu Wen, has reported the incident to the county government, requesting that personnel be sent to assess the extent of the damage and that motorized rowing boats be regulated to ensure the safety of passengers.

Xu Yabo Case Results in Guilty Verdict: Following the conclusion of arguments in the Xu Yabo theft case on the 19th, a sentence of seven years of imprisonment was pronounced on the morning of the 23rd. Xu Yabo declared in court that he was dissatisfied and would appeal.

Suzhou 90

Merchants Oppose the Rectification of the Business Tax Law: After the County Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the provincial government regarding the Jiangsu Province's rectification of business tax methods, which violated ministerial orders, a reply was received yesterday stating: "An investigation reveals that the business tax in this province has not been diligently handled by various bureaus, and declarations by shops have not been accurate. Therefore, a thorough rectification is necessary. The Changshu Chamber of Commerce's proposal to temporarily maintain the tax rate should be thoroughly rectified. Given the lack of proper business tax management, the Chamber of Commerce should consider the overall situation and assist in the rectification. Objections to the rectification methods are unwarranted. The request is denied." Yesterday (the 23rd) morning, the Chamber convened a general meeting of representatives from various industries, which resulted in the following: (1) Unanimous rejection of the Jiangsu Province's rectification of business tax methods. (2) A request to the Tax Bureau to postpone the collection of the third-term tax payment due to the current downturn in business. (3) A unanimous effort to prevent the Tax Bureau from directly investigating various businesses.

Soldier Huang Jixing Kills Squad Leader: The battalion headquarters of the Second Battalion, Sixth Regiment, 120th Brigade, 60th Division, stationed in Hupi Gong Temple in Suzhou, had a private first-class soldier named Huang Jixing. Yesterday (the 23rd) at 2:00 PM, while on guard duty, Huang shot and killed Squad Leader Zheng Wenbiao with a rifle. The battalion immediately detained Huang Jixing, bound him, and sent him to the regimental headquarters for transfer to the divisional headquarters for investigation. According to Huang, his father had previously been killed by Zheng Wenbiao, and this was an act of revenge for his father.

Three Legal Groups Request the Cancellation of Additional Land Tax: The agricultural, commercial, and educational legal groups of Wu County, recognizing that the people are unable to bear the continued imposition of additional land value tax by the Suzhou authorities, jointly petitioned the provincial government, appealing for the cancellation of the tax to restore public trust.

Wuxi 91

True Account of Robbery Now Clear: Hu Xianchu, a clerk at the Sensheng Soybean Cake and Cottonseed Shop outside the North Gate of Sanli Bridge, Wuxi, went to Shanghai to collect 1,950 yuan from the Yuanda Oil Firm. Upon returning to Wuxi, he claimed that the funds had been robbed by three bandits. It is now known that the truth of this case has been fully revealed. It turns out that the shop's manager, Wang Shufan, had sent Hu Xianchu to Shanghai to collect the funds on the 10th of this month. After collecting the money, Hu went to the exchange to trade and gamble, intending to profit from the principal. However, his efforts were unsuccessful, and he lost all the funds. Because Hu had not returned to Wuxi after several days, manager Wang Shufan wrote to the Yuanda Oil Firm in Shanghai to inquire. The firm replied that Hu had collected the full amount on the 18th. After receiving the letter, Wang went to Shanghai the day before yesterday to search for Hu. He found Hu but did not mention the funds. They then took the night train back to Wuxi together. After getting off the train, Wang Shufan returned to the shop first, and Hu Xianchu then took a rickshaw back to the shop. Nearing the shop, Hu, with no other option, fabricated the story of the robbery. Upon learning the truth, Shufan was furious and wanted to send Hu to the authorities. However, after repeated pleas from Hu's relatives, Wang agreed to accept compensation of 500 yuan, with 300 yuan paid upfront and a promissory note for the remaining 100 yuan to be repaid on schedule.

The Case of Selling Japanese Coal Causes a Great Disturbance: Regarding the Yitaixing Coal Company's sale of Japanese coal, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association previously resolved to inquire with the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Association about how to handle the Japanese coal and published a notice about the case. Later, the student association proposed a reconsideration, arguing that severe punishment was necessary. Yesterday, the committee re-resolved to confiscate all the coal found and impose a double penalty. After the meeting, it was noted that a reporter from the Xin Wuxi Bao, Zhou Hanru, had published a warning to the members of the Anti-Japanese Association, suggesting that Yitaixing had engaged in bribery but without naming specific individuals, which was considered detrimental to their reputation. It was decided that Zhou Hanru and Yan Yunqiao, the manager of Yitaixing Coal Company, should be brought to the meeting for questioning to clarify the truth. The prosecutor's office summoned Yan Yunqiao and Zhou Hanru to the Anti-Japanese Association that evening, where they were questioned severely. Yan Yunqiao claimed that the coal had already been sold to the Gansheng Silk Factory and had nothing to do with him, so there was no reason for bribery. Zhou Hanru said that she had heard it as a rumor and could not name anyone but hoped that all staff members would be clean. The final result was that Yao Xinchui and Li Xin'yan of the Anti-Japanese Association stated that a letter of proof from the Gansheng Silk Factory was needed before a resolution could be reached. As the meeting was adjourning, Zhou Hanru's rickshaw puller suddenly clashed with staff members of the Anti-Japanese Association, and a scuffle broke out, resulting in injuries on both sides. They were taken to the Public Security Bureau to examine the injuries and request legal action.

Changshu 92

Mei Kun Ferry Runs Aground and Sinks: Hupu Meili in this county is an important town in the east of the county, and the market is quite lively. Recently, someone organized a Mei Kun ferry service, from Hupu Meili to Kunshan. On the 21st of this month, the company's Linfeng ferry was sailing from Kunshan to Changshu when it ran aground near Ayu Kou, close to the river. Because the tugboat was too heavy, the bottom of the boat hit a reef (some say it hit the bridge pier), causing a hole in the bottom. The passengers were very alarmed. The tugboat was cut, and the passengers were ferried ashore, but soon the ferry sank to the bottom. Fortunately, no passengers were injured. Later, the tugboat sailed two li away and landed the passengers ashore. They telegraphed the company to send another ferry to rescue them.

Jiangyin 93

Strictly Prohibiting Racketeering: Huangtiangang, north of Jiangyin, is a vital thoroughfare connecting the Yangtze River to the interior. In recent years, due to the abolition of tariffs, unemployed vagrants have gathered in the port, colluding with a few corrupt officials to extort money from passing cargo ships under the guise of "pai dang" (wharf management). This was reported to the provincial government, which sent an investigator who confirmed the allegations. In addition to recording a major demerit for the officials involved, including Li Jialin, the director of the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau (who has since been dismissed), and Zhu Tianqi, the district chief of the First District, County Magistrate Ma was ordered to expel the five ringleaders, Tang Lian, Jin Yuanlang, Huang Rongquan, Pan Kunlin, and Pan Lingeng, and to issue a public notice strictly prohibiting such racketeering. It was also proposed to properly manage the water gates and maintain navigation to Huangtiangang for approval. After receiving the order, County Magistrate Ma instructed the Public Security Bureau and the District Office to review the matter together with the party and government conversation meeting, and submit a report.

Chief of Public Security Jiang Resigns: Jiang Guang, the chief of public security, has been in office for several months. Recently, due to the difficulties of his work, he submitted his resignation to the county government and the political office the other day. It is unknown whether it will be approved.

Nantong 94

Yuzhang Torpedo Boat Runs Aground and Sinks: On the 21st, at 4:00 PM, the Yuzhang torpedo boat was sailing from Rengang to Jiangyin when it ran aground on a reef near Xinjiegang, Changyinsha, outside Lujinggang, due to fog. The boat immediately sank. There were 76 officers and soldiers on board. Fortunately, the Daqing steamer was sailing upstream and rescued all of them. 50 people were sent to Lujinggang, and 26 were ferried to Changyinsha. On the 22nd, they crossed the river to Nantong. The Yingrui warship happened to be sailing from Jiangyin, and the officers and soldiers boarded it. Only a few rifles were taken from the boat; the rest of the military supplies could not be moved out. Before disembarking, 40 tons of coal were loaded. Currently, only the mast is visible above the water. Commander Ren of the boat is still on vacation. Commander Lin Yuanquan of the Yingrui warship has telegraphed the Naval Department and will send salvage engineers to work.

The Yiyu District Snatches Bandit Organization: The Yiyu District in the east of Nantong has recently experienced rampant banditry. After police and militia searched, on the 22nd, a bandit organization was smashed, and bandit leaders Zhang Kui, as well as notorious bandits Qian Guangxiang, Wang Shishan, Zhang Taoliang, Jiang Zhaofang, and Liang Hanli, were arrested, along with two large jars of bullets. They were sent to the county government that day. After interrogation by the Pacification Military Court, they confessed to hiding a large number of rifles and Mauser pistols in the fields, and they were taken to excavate them.

Dispute Over Reclamation of Pastureland for Educational Purposes Resolved: The Haimen County Education Bureau applied to Tongyi for the reclamation of pastureland for educational purposes. After a final ruling by the Ministry of Education, 90 shares of the reclamation and pasture company, totaling 1,980 mu of land, were allocated to Haimen. The two counties have sent commissioners to allocate the land and close the case.

Lu Si Pirates Occupy Sanjia Town: Pirate ships from Lu Si have been gathering in increasing numbers in recent days. 300 pirates invaded Sanjia Town on the 21st, and merchants and residents fled in droves. The pirates extorted money from fishermen and, when their demands were not met, set fire to their boats. There have also been cases of bandits looting in nearby towns and villages.

Zhenjiang 95

Pretending to Borrow a Name to Obtain Housing: The Runjin Bathhouse at the entrance of Baota Lane in this city was jointly established by Bu Rongshou and Hu Fengkui, residents from other regions. Recently, because they did not want to continue operating, they advertised for sale. However, Feng Shishun, who had previously served as a runner in the county government, colluded with Wang Zhihe and pretended to buy the property in the name of a certain director. They stated that the housing and business assets totaled 16,000 yuan and agreed to exchange the silver contract by the end of the 11th lunar month. If a breach of contract occurred, the breaching party would be fined 2,000 yuan as compensation. However, by the due date, Wang only made excuses and procrastinated. Until around the 20th of this month, he only paid 4,000 yuan and used words to drive away the contract. He started practicing that day, agreeing that after Director Mou reviewed the contract the next day, the remaining money would be paid in full. However, the next day, Wang avoided meeting, and Feng continued to make excuses. Until yesterday, when Bu negotiated with him, Feng first used Director Mou's name to intimidate him and then resorted to violence to suppress him. When the police intervened, he even wanted to insult the police. Many passersby were very dissatisfied, so he was taken to the Fifth Sub-bureau. The outcome of this case is still unknown.

Court Investigates Case of Two Police Captains: Zhang Peifu, the police captain of Gaoyou, and Xia Yuanhu, the captain of the water patrol, were previously suspected of colluding with bandits. The Department of Civil Affairs ordered Cheng Zhuang, the district chief of the Fifth Water Police District, to arrest them and send them to the province, where they were held in the company headquarters of the Special Service Camp. They were transferred to the Zhenjiang Local Court the other day. Yesterday, the prosecutor of the court interrogated them and ordered each to pay 200 yuan in cash and find a guarantor to be released pending investigation. However, it is said that Zhang Peifu was unwilling to accept this and submitted a document and a certificate of no crime to the Department of Civil Affairs, requesting a thorough investigation.

Foremen Surround Section Chief Demanding Payment: The Zhenjiang Dakoumen River Filling Project was contracted to Dong Yiming, Yan Guangzu, and others, who stipulated that the total amount of earthwork was 18,200 square meters, with a price of 1.5 yuan per square meter. According to the contract, 80% would be paid, and the remaining 20% would be kept as a deposit until the project was completed and inspected. Work began in March of last year, and over the past few months, a total of over 15,000 square meters of earthwork have been completed, and Dong and others have received payment for the earthwork on time from the Construction Department. Recently, Dong and others suddenly claimed that they wanted to dismiss the workers and insisted on receiving the 20% deposit. The Construction Department refused to allow this because it did not comply with the contract stipulations. Yesterday afternoon, Dong and others took advantage of Section Chief Xu of the Third Section of the department returning to his residence for lunch and led dozens of foremen and workers to surround Xu's residence, shouting loudly. Fortunately, the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau heard the news and sent many police officers to suppress them, and Dong and others dispersed.

Yangzhou 96

Chen Zheng State Robbery Case Solved and Culprit Apprehended: The home of Chen Zheng in Yangshou Dam, Zhu Gong Temple, in the western countryside was robbed some time ago, and the bandits set fire, killing the owner and injuring three others. Two of the bandits were also injured and taken away by the bandits. The Public Security Bureau's Detective Team, led by informants Shan Zhaonan and detectives Hu Kaiyin, went to Shaobo the other day (21st) and arrested Zhang Yuwu, one of the injured bandits involved in the Chen case. He confessed without hesitation and confessed to many other cases and accomplices.

Xiaoshan 97

Exhumation of Corpse to Investigate Filicide Case: A farmer named Wei Amao, whose son A Shun lived in Zhangliang Bridge, eight li from Xiaoshan, did not do his job, but gambled all day. On the night of the 18th, he asked his father for silver dollars, which angered the old father, who used a firewood stick to smash his son's head. Brain matter flowed out and he died. The next day, he was hastily coffined and buried in Yizhong. The neighbors nearby heard the news and reported it to the county government and the county court. On the 20th, the prosecutor arrived to exhume the corpse. He examined the head of the corpse, which was bloody and the brain matter flowing, and confirmed that he had been beaten to death. Wei Amao, who was over seventy years old, was not believed to have been so heavy-handed, so his brother Shunyang was summoned for questioning. However, because he had already fled, it was suspected that he had helped beat him. The neighbors were also summoned for questioning, but there was no definite evidence. After the examination, he returned to the court, filed a public prosecution, and issued a summons to his brother and parents for interrogation.

Rioters Loot Changming Village: The Freedom Kong Village in Linpu Changming Village, Xiaoshan, was surrounded and looted by more than 50 rioters from Tianle Village, a neighboring county, the other day. More than 20 houses and dozens of thatched sheds were burned down. Jiang's young daughter was burned to death, and four owners were shot and killed. The loss was between 40,000 and 50,000 yuan. After the rioters were satisfied with looting, they returned to their old nest. On the 20th, County Magistrate Lin Yuanquan and Public Security Director Zheng Xin led the entire police team to Linpu for inspection.

Educational News

Important News

Ministry of Education Investigates Secondary Schools Nationwide 98

The Ministry of Education is currently investigating the general situation of public and private secondary schools nationwide and has re-issued a form to be distributed to education departments in all provinces and cities.

An investigation of secondary school names and distribution nationwide has been completed by the Ministry. A copy is being sent out to you for your information. Secondary education facilities in each province and city should be inspected to determine the state of affairs and adjust to the needs of the local environment, seeking adaptation and progress. Because the compilation of these statistics was rushed, the contents are too brief. A simplified survey form for public and private secondary schools in each province and city is being issued. Departments are to complete the forms according to the standards, and those that need to be forwarded to the subordinate schools for inquiry should be handled quickly. All forms must be completed and submitted to the Ministry before mid-March for further compilation and printing.

Highlights of Ministry of Education's Work Over the Past Year 99

The Ministry of Education recently released a review of its work over the past year. It is very long. The main points are excerpted below. (1) Promoting Party Ideology Education (such as certifying Party Ideology teachers and deans of students, passing draft standards for Party Ideology courses, reviewing Party Ideology textbooks for primary and secondary schools, and editing a "Thousand Character Primer" on the Three Principles of the People for adults and children; currently, it is working on a "Thousand Character Primer" on the Three Principles of the People for rural use). (2) Promoting academic research, such as expanding academic research institutions (universities with research institutes include Zhongshan, Peking, and Tsinghua Universities; academic organizations registered in accordance with regulations include the Chinese Economic Society, the Chinese Agricultural Society, the Forestry Society, the Academic Research Association, the Chinese Meteorological Society, the Statistical Society, the Metrology Society, and twenty-two others); rewarding academic talent (formulating measures for academic research internships and scholarships and for the state to provide printing subsidies for scholars to publish academic monographs); translating scientific terms (the translations of pharmaceutical terms are largely finalized; terms for mathematics, physics, chemistry, biology, economics, society, psychology, and education are being translated); establishing the Central Education Museum to focus on science education and preserving ancient books. (3) Reorganizing higher education, such as revising the system of colleges and specialized schools (abolishing the regulation for single-discipline universities and dividing universities into colleges of arts, sciences, law, education, agriculture, industry, and medicine; only those with three or more colleges may be called universities, otherwise, they are called independent colleges); changing specialized schools to vocational schools to teach applied sciences and train technical personnel; reorganizing public and private universities and specialized schools (1. Appropriately increasing the budget and ensuring funding; 2. Expanding facilities; 3. Focusing on teacher qualifications, improving teacher salaries, and restricting teachers from teaching multiple courses; 4. Strictly defining curricula and emphasizing experimentation; 5. Appropriately establishing scholarships and fellowships; 6. Designating Peking and Central Universities to establish Mongolian and Tibetan classes; 7. Establishing measures to provide preferential treatment to overseas Chinese students in national universities; 8. National universities establishing university education promotion committees); private universities that are considered qualified for operation are allowed to register, while those that are not are ordered to close. Currently, there are sixty-eight public and private universities and independent colleges in the country, excluding private schools that have been ordered to close: seventeen national, twenty provincial, and thirty-one private. There are forty universities and twenty-eight independent colleges. In addition, there are several private universities that have not been registered. Apart from the law schools that have been ordered to close, there are eleven specialized schools: two national, thirteen provincial, and five private. In addition, there are several schools that have not been registered); compiling curricula and equipment standards (planning to promulgate regulations nationwide in the twenty-first year); (4) Reorganizing overseas study affairs, such as investigating the status of students studying abroad and restricting measures for students studying abroad; (5) Reorganizing secondary education (secondary schools). In the summer of the twentieth year, the Committee for the Compilation of Course and Equipment Standards for Primary and Secondary Schools was established, and the original Committee for the Drafting of Course Standards for Primary and Secondary Schools was ended. The official course standards for junior and senior high schools will be promulgated soon. The Committee for the Compilation of Training Standards for Primary and Secondary Schools is studying methods, and the Training Standards will be promulgated soon. In addition, strict methods for training secondary school students are being developed in the hope of bringing young people onto the right track and fostering a simple academic style. Over one hundred textbooks for secondary schools have been reviewed and approved, over fifty have not been approved, and one hundred and ten have been revised. Over forty extracurricular reading materials for secondary schools have been approved for publication; (Normal Schools) A provisional standard for high school normal school courses has been formulated and promulgated nationwide. The Second National Education Conference of the National Education Association discussed and revised the national education program, which contains a comprehensive plan for improving normal education, with rural education occupying an important position; (Vocational Schools) The junior high school curriculum standard stipulates that crafts are to be taught and each school is to choose from agriculture, industry, or home economics depending on their own circumstances. Vocational elective subjects, from five to fifteen credits, were also introduced to cultivate students' professional preparation. The high school commercial course curriculum standard has been promulgated for vocational schools other than secondary schools. The agricultural, industrial, and home economics courses are being compiled. After completion, the curriculum standards for primary vocational schools will be compiled. In the summer of the twentieth year, the Vocational Education Design Committee was established. All plans for vocational education facilities will be studied and reviewed by the committee, and the measures will be implemented in order; (Investigation of the General Situation of Secondary Education) (To be continued)

Detailed Record of the British Boxer Indemnity Board of Trustees 100

The seventh meeting of the British Boxer Indemnity Board of Trustees was held in Beijing last week, and this newspaper briefly reported on it at the time. Because the minutes had not been reviewed by the trustees, the details were not published. Now that the minutes have been revised, important resolutions are recorded below: (1) The Loan Repayment Method was revised and passed. From now on, the loans of each agency must be handled in accordance with these methods. (2) The applications of educational and cultural institutions were resolved to be temporarily not discussed until interest is received. (3) The four applications for Boxer Indemnity funds by the Construction Committee of the Ministry of Railways were resolved to be submitted to the Technical Committee for review before being submitted to the Finance Committee for review. (4) The existing British pound Boxer Indemnity funds will be converted into national currency. (5) Hang Liwu was appointed as the Director-General of the Board of Trustees' office. It is also heard that the conference will hold its eighth meeting at the end of next month.

This City

Emergency Meeting of Various Middle School Students' Anti-Japanese Associations 101

Assistance to Workers on Strike for Anti-Japanese Resistance

Declaration Released: Resisting Japan to the End

Letter Sent to Qixiu and Shanghai Baptist University: Do Not Suppress Students

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation United Association of students from various middle schools in this city held its 11th emergency meeting of the second session of the executive committee at its office in Jiping Lane, Ximen, yesterday at 2:00 PM. Representatives from twelve schools, including Pudong, Datong, Quanzhang, Hui, Qixiu, Shanghai High School of the Provincial Government, Guanghua, Chengzhong, the attached middle school of Chizhi, Jingye, Aiguo, and Wuben, attended. Ding Dezhao from Hui School and Yang Xikun from Shanghai High School recorded the minutes. Report items: (omitted).

Matters for discussion: 1) The People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation United Association requested assistance from this association for workers on strike for anti-Japanese resistance and for volunteer soldiers. It was resolved that this association has dispatched an investigation team to conduct an investigation. 2) The People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation United Association and this association initiated a memorial service for the innocent Chinese constables who were killed. It was resolved to send two representatives to discuss the matter. 3) Sending representatives to participate in the preparatory committee for the memorial service. It was resolved to send representatives from Guanghua and Shanghai High School. 4) Stipulating the rules of procedure for this association. It was resolved that the standing executive committee would be responsible for drafting them. 5) If the various divisions fail to work diligently, this association should elect representatives from each division to lead and supervise them. The resolution was passed. Shanghai High School was assigned to the document division, Guanghua to the general affairs division, Wuben to the publicity division, Chizhi to the military training division, and Jingye to the inspection division. 6) Dongwu No. 2 Middle School's membership rights have been suspended. This association should elect another military training division representative to fill the vacancy. It was resolved to submit the matter to the representative assembly for discussion. 7) Increasing the number of regular meetings of this association. It was resolved to add one meeting on Tuesdays. 8) Shanghai Baptist University authorities are using various unintentional means to undermine the patriotic movement. How should this association deal with this issue? It was resolved that this association would issue a written warning and publicly condemn them to deter others from following suit. It was also reported that the association issued an important declaration due to the suppression of the patriotic movement by the authorities of various schools. Furthermore, it sent letters to the principals of Qixiu and Shanghai Baptist University, requesting that they not obstruct the anti-Japanese work of the students in their schools, so as to facilitate its progress. The text of the documents is recorded below:

Important Declaration: Ever since the September 18th Incident occurred, all Chinese compatriots with even a little bit of courage have been filled with righteous indignation and have risen up to save themselves. We, the young students, as intellectuals, are inherently responsible for awakening the masses and leading the masses. Moreover, under the current circumstances, how can we stand by idly? Therefore, we have been running around, shouting, crying until our voices are hoarse. However, the authorities are willing to be lackeys of imperialism, sacrificing national sovereignty in exchange for the pleasure of imperialism and to achieve their personal goals of territorial division. The news of the neutralization of Jinzhou and the joint administration of Tianjin has broken the hearts of us students. Reaching this point, how can we continue to peacefully study and trust this traitorous government? Therefore, at the cost of any sacrifice, we have followed the principle that if the skin is gone, what will the hair cling to? We have unanimously gone on strike to oppose treason and awaken our compatriots. We have endured great hardships. However, the government authorities continue to wantonly suppress our youth's anti-Japanese movement and add the evil name of "rioters." We have long understood their treachery and are not surprised. We only grieve for the difficult fate of our Chinese nation. However, the authorities of various schools have even become insane and willing to be the hawks and hounds of traitors, deliberately undermining the patriotic movement of the youth. They even arbitrarily accuse enthusiastic students and frequently expel them, wanting to place patriotic youth in dire straits. Alas! The aggression of imperialism has not ceased, and the running dogs of imperialism continue to roar. However, the educators who are supposed to guide our pure youth are willing to be running dogs of running dogs, directly undermining our youth. It is truly heartbreaking. This association, on behalf of more than 100,000 middle school students, solemnly declares: If there are those who are willing to act as hawks and hounds, undermining our youth's anti-Japanese national salvation movement, this association, in order to carry out its original purpose of anti-Japanese national salvation, will use all its strength to deal with these obstacles to anti-Japanese resistance, at the cost of any sacrifice. We hereby declare!

Letter to Two Schools: The association sent a letter to Qixiu and Shanghai Baptist University, which stated: "Respectfully addressed, Ever since Japan's invasion and occupation of the Northeast, several days have passed. They have spared no effort in damaging our sovereignty and slaughtering our people. However, our national border defense officials have adopted a policy of non-resistance, and important figures in the party-state have maintained a calm attitude. Furthermore, the general public, due to a lack of education and the oppression of the government, is unaware of the national crisis. Only a small number of students are running around, calling out, and working hard for national salvation. However, students are still in their learning years, and all aspects of their anti-Japanese work should be guided by the education community. Since anti-Japanese work is aimed at seeking happiness for the future of the nation, the education community should actively promote and guide it. However, according to investigations, we have heard that your principal has been obstructing the anti-Japanese work of the students in various ways and has even suggested that "if they continue to engage in anti-Japanese work, they will be expelled." This association bears the responsibility of leading middle school students in the entire city and cannot sit idly by. Therefore, we are writing to request that your principal immediately withdraw this order in order to facilitate the progress of anti-Japanese work.

New Plan for Chinese Children's Elementary School 103
