Original Text of the Municipal Government's Protest Against the Incident of Japanese Residents Causing Trouble on North Sichuan Road 118

The Municipal Government has lodged a protest with the Japanese Consul-General regarding the disturbance caused by the crowd at the Japanese Residents' General Assembly on the 20th along North Sichuan Road, where shops were smashed. The original text is copied below: Respectfully addressed, According to the report submitted by the Municipal Public Security Bureau, at 1:00 PM on the 20th of this month, Japanese residents of this city held a general assembly at the Japanese Residents' Club on Peng Road in the Public Concession. Approximately one thousand people attended the meeting. After the meeting, they went to the Japanese Consulate-General in Shanghai and the Japanese Naval Landing Force to petition. While passing along North Sichuan Road, they caused disturbances along the way, smashing many shops and damaging the windows of tram number 125 and public buses in the concession. Upon reaching the Qiujiang Road intersection, they wantonly destroyed the glass windows of Chinese shops. It was not until after 6:00 PM that they dispersed on Dixiwei Road. At that time, the people of this city were filled with uncontrollable anger. Fortunately, the head of the district, along with the police team leader and police officers, exerted great efforts to suppress and persuade them, and no accidents occurred. The losses suffered by the various Chinese shops this time are extremely large. In view of this, regarding this illegal action by the Japanese residents, the Municipal Government has repeatedly sent letters to your Consul-General, requesting attention and effective prohibition. However, this time, the Japanese residents have again deliberately provoked trouble. At this time of serious crisis and heightened public sentiment, if misunderstandings occur, the responsibility will naturally rest with you. Therefore, we hereby lodge a protest, requesting that your Consul-General quickly investigate the perpetrators, punish them according to law, and strictly prevent the recurrence of such incidents in the future. Regarding the amount of losses suffered by each shop, we will request compensation after a detailed investigation. A corresponding letter is hereby sent, requesting your attention to the matter and a reply.

The Situation of the Japanese Riot Case Remains Extremely Serious 119

Wu Tiecheng Discusses the Sino-Japanese Negotiations

The Municipal Government Is Scheduled to Respond to the Japanese Protest Tomorrow

Our Country's Protest Has Not Yet Received a Response from the Japanese Side

Demands of the Japanese Residents' Assembly

Regarding the situation of the Sino-Japanese negotiations in Shanghai, Mayor Wu stated yesterday that the municipal government is preparing to respond to the Japanese Consul-General's protest of the 21st tomorrow. The protest submitted by the municipal government on the 22nd has not yet received a response. He also stated that the message of condolence from the Japanese fleet commander was not accurate, but yesterday five more Japanese warships arrived in Shanghai at 3:30 PM and anchored in the Yangshupu River. Yesterday, due to the Japanese holding a residents' assembly, the Chinese concession authorities temporarily imposed martial law as a precaution. The situation remains extremely serious. The continued developments are recorded in detail below:

Responding to the Japanese Protest Tomorrow Mayor of this city, Wu Tiecheng, returned to Shanghai yesterday morning after traveling to Beijing some days prior. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency visited the municipal government at 3:00 PM yesterday to understand the progress of the Sino-Japanese negotiations. He was granted an audience and made the following statement: "During my trip to Beijing, I only reported to the central government about the deterioration of the situation between the Chinese and Japanese people in Shanghai. I did not engage in concrete discussions. As for the protest letter submitted by Japanese Consul-General Kuramatsu Murai on the 21st regarding the injury of five Japanese monks in Yinxiang Township on the 18th, we are currently preparing a response. Although the specific content of the response has not yet been determined, considering the four points raised by the Japanese consul, the first, second, and third points can generally be considered for handling. As for the fourth point, which demands the suppression of anti-Japanese movements and the disbandment of anti-Japanese organizations, since these organizations are formed by the people based on their spontaneous patriotic sincerity, as long as their actions are within a reasonable scope and do not hinder local order and tranquility, the government cannot suppress them with political power. Therefore, I stated when the Japanese Consul-General came to the municipal government to submit the protest letter that we have no right to suppress them. However, if their actions go beyond the bounds and are found to be illegal, hindering local order and tranquility, the municipal government will definitely impose sanctions according to the law." The response is scheduled to be delivered to the Japanese Consul-General next Monday (the 25th).

The Japanese Consul Has Not Yet Responded However, the protest letter submitted by our side on the 22nd has not yet received a reply as of this evening (the 23rd). However, when the Japanese Consul-General expressed his regret to me the other day (the 21st), he stated that he would strictly arrest the ronin who burned down the Sanyou Industrial Factory and severely punish them according to Japanese law.

The Ultimatum Is Not Accurate He continued by saying that in the past two days, Chinese and foreign newspapers have published that on Thursday night, Rear Admiral Shiozawa, commander of the First Japanese Fleet stationed in China, sent a message of condolence to me, demanding an immediate and satisfactory reply to the anti-Japanese movement by the Chinese and the assault on Japanese residents. I can solemnly declare that as of 4:00 PM today (the 23rd), that is, at the time of this meeting with you, I have not received such a document. Moreover, while diplomatic relations still exist, all interactions between China and Japan in Shanghai should be addressed on one side to the Mayor of the Shanghai Municipal Government and on the other to the Consul-General of the Japanese Consulate. Therefore, it is not reasonable for the Japanese fleet commander to send a letter directly to me.

We Will Adopt Legitimate Defense The reporter also asked what the Mayor thought if the Japanese disregarded everything and engaged in large-scale disturbances. He replied, "The central government has already issued orders that if anyone invades inland territory, we will adopt legitimate defense. Moreover, we have already made considerable preparations for maintaining security in Shanghai. If anything happens, we will take the necessary measures."

We Should Handle It Calmly However, regarding these provocative incidents by Japanese ronin, both the government and the people should handle them calmly in order to eliminate them invisibly. As the saying goes, "Seeing something strange and not being surprised, the strangeness will disappear by itself." The Japanese ronin fear nothing more than our disarray. If we alarm each other, we will give them an opportunity. However, when I (Wu, referring to himself) say handle it calmly, I do not mean that we should allow them to commit violence and disturbances. If they commit illegal violence and disturbances against us, we should sanction them through legitimate procedures.

The Municipal Government's Policy of Peace In short, the municipal government's policy for dealing with these disputes is to prioritize peaceful resolution.

The Chinese Concession Has Always Cooperated After the Japanese ronin burned down the Sanyou Industrial Factory, various organizations requested that more military police be sent to assist the Municipal Council in maintaining local security. Mayor Wu stated yesterday that the municipal government has always cooperated with the Municipal Council in maintaining local security, but sending military police to the concession seems to be difficult in reality.

Strict Precautions in the Chinese Area The Chinese area police authorities also took very strict precautions yesterday. The Public Security Bureau had previously received an order from the Garrison Command, instructing them to strictly guard against it yesterday. Director Wen ordered all police officers in the five districts to be armed and dispatched. More than 100 police officers from the Second Police Platoon were sent to Zhabei to patrol very secretly to the Chinese area near Sichuan Road, Tiantong'an Road, Baoxing Road, Baoshan Road, and Jiangwan Road. The precautions were even more severe in this area. The Garrison Command also transferred a large number of troops to suppress the area. Although martial law was not announced at night, patrols were extremely secretive.

Martial Law in the Concession Yesterday The Public Concession authorities paid attention because Japanese people publicized that they would hold a residents' assembly at Peng Road at 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon. Therefore, the Municipal Council specially notified 12 locations in the Concession, including the Central Gordon, Xinzha, Putuo Road, Jing'an Temple, Harbin, Hongkou, Huisi, Huishan, Dixiwei Road, and Yangshupu, to implement strict precautions and sent all Chinese and Western detectives to patrol outside. Red police vehicles were also driven to various important institutions to protect them.

Japanese Residents' Assembly The Japanese residents of Shanghai held a residents' assembly at the Japanese Club at 69 Peng Road at 3:30 PM yesterday afternoon. Kuramatsu Murai, the Japanese Consul stationed in Shanghai, feared that ronin would secretly bring weapons and take action after the meeting. He specially joined the Japanese patrol officers of the Public Concession Police Department to inspect the residents' assembly venue. More than 1,500 Japanese people participated. The chairman first reported the purpose of the meeting. The atmosphere at the venue was unusually tense. Later, the Japanese Consul arrived at the meeting to explain that arson and burning down the Sanyou Company factory were quite inappropriate. If they acted freely, the incident would inevitably escalate. He hoped that they would not act without authorization, and those who violated this would be punished by the consul. Therefore, all the people accepted the Japanese consul's advice, but demanded that the consul should negotiate with the Chinese authorities to achieve a satisfactory result. The meeting finally adjourned at 4:30 PM.

Japanese Held a Memorial Service At 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon, the Japanese held a memorial service for Liangse Songshilang at the Japanese Temple on Zhapu Road, Hongkou. Various Japanese groups stationed in China sent wreaths and other gifts. The meeting closed at 3:00 PM. The funeral committee then loaded the coffin onto a car, and prepared 45 cars for the mourners to ride in. It was carried to the Japanese Cemetery at 722 Yokohama Road for cremation. The cremation was completed at 3:45 PM.

Seven Japanese Confessed According to an investigation by a reporter from the Huadong News Agency, seven suspects who burned down the Eryou Company factory have confessed to the Japanese consulate. The list of their names is recorded below: ㈠ Guangcun Fangcang, 46 years old, resident of No. A-1, Haining Road, this city. ㈡ Hosoya Yuichiro, 31 years old, resident of No. A-10, Haining Road, this city. ㈢ Yuan Dingci, 32 years old, resident of No. 103, Qiujiang Road. ㈣ Guan Heng Taro, 28 years old, resident of Jiugengli, Peng Road. ㈤ Kinoshita Kanzo, 40 years old, resident of No. 1018, Zhan'anli, Wusong Road. ㈥ Mori Masanobu, 16 years old, resident of No. 2, Mingdaoli, Shiqing Road. ㈦ Kitatsuji Takuji, 23 years old, resident of No. 97, Doule'an Road. The above seven people were escorted back to Osaka by the Japanese consulate yesterday for legal punishment.

Japanese Attitude Towards the Concession 120

Japanese Official Expresses Deep Apologies to the Municipal Council According to news from the Municipal Council, regarding the incident that occurred last Wednesday morning near Ward Road between Japanese residents and Chinese patrol officers of the Municipal Council, which resulted in the death of one patrol officer and one Japanese resident, and several injuries on both sides, the chairman reported at the Municipal Council meeting on Wednesday that the Japanese Consul-General visited the bureau that afternoon and expressed his deep regret for the incident. He also stated that he would discuss compensation for the deceased and injured patrol officers with the chairman, and informed the chairman that he would take necessary measures to punish those who attacked the patrol officers. Japanese Director Fukushima also expressed regret over the incident and assured the board that the Japanese officials did not sympathize with the Japanese Youth League that incited the incident.

Japanese Do Not Wish to Invade the Neutral Concession According to the Zi Lin Bao, the first person to visit the Japanese Consul-General in Shanghai yesterday morning was Major General Macnaghten, Chairman of the Municipal Council. It is reported that the discussions between Macnaghten and Japanese Consul-General Murai included Shiozawa's naval commander's declaration, but the results were not announced. Also, Macnaghten and Fessenden, Director-General of the Municipal Council, visited Commander Shiozawa together yesterday morning to discuss the so-called Japanese "Message of Condolence". Shiozawa said that he would not take any action in the concession without first notifying the Municipal Council authorities, and that the Japanese now want to stop anti-Japanese activities in Shanghai, and obtain a satisfactory reply from the Chinese authorities to the Japanese Consul-General's request. The Japanese do not wish to invade the neutrality of the Public Concession, or interfere with the Municipal Council's efforts to maintain the laws and regulations of the Concession.

Japanese Military Officer Responds Ambiguously to Foreign Media Representative According to the Da Mei Evening News, a representative of the Da Mei Evening News visited the Japanese Fleet Commander Shiozawa this morning (the 23rd). A certain military officer met with the representative on his behalf and stated that the Japanese hoped that the Chinese authorities would have a satisfactory response to Shiozawa's request made yesterday. If they did not comply with the request, the Japanese Navy would take appropriate direct action. When the representative asked what the so-called appropriate direct action meant, the officer did not answer, but said that the Japanese Navy stationed in Shanghai would not take extraordinary actions today.

Da Mei Evening News on Maintaining Peace in Shanghai 121

Its Root is Planted in the Liaoning Case

Intimidation Is of No Use

No Need to Increase Defensive Forces

The Da Mei Evening News editorial states that Shanghai does not need to increase the defensive forces of China and Japan. Increasing troops will not stop the incident, but will easily incite it. Tokyo views the recent Shanghai dispute as a local incident and orders local officials to resolve it. This move is appropriate, but the Navy Ministry's order to send warships to Shanghai is inconsistent with this attitude. Now it is not necessary to send marines to Shanghai as ordered by the Navy Ministry, and China does not need to send defensive forces to the Public Concession as requested by the Chinese Taxpayers Association. The protection of the Public Concession is the responsibility of the Shanghai Municipal Council. Maintaining peace in Shanghai is extremely difficult today. If the existing law and order agencies are arbitrarily increased, we dare to believe that it will increase the harm that is being curbed. Therefore, armed Japanese soldiers or Chinese soldiers arriving in Shanghai is enough to provoke. The current situation requires a psychological response. If we show off our military strength, it may ignite a prairie fire, which is very worrying. The police of the Public Concession are now doing their best to fulfill their responsibilities. We sincerely hope that the negotiations between Chinese and Japanese officials will not further stir up resentment. Although this incident is local in nature, its roots are planted in the Liaoning case. Tokyo should not ignore this point. We dare not believe that the root cause is not mentioned, and it is said that the final result can be obtained by making a request. Moreover, this kind of request, aided by military intimidation, can be called an extremely risky means today. This newspaper has always disapproved of the methods used by Chinese people to boycott Japanese goods, but this is completely different from the Japanese request for "guaranteeing that Chinese groups or individuals will no longer have anti-Japanese movements in the future". As long as resentment exists, Chinese people will boycott Japan one day, which is beyond doubt. Intimidation is of no use, but will increase anger. Chinese and Japanese people must maintain peace in Shanghai. Anyone who violates the laws and regulations, regardless of their nationality, should be punished. However, the root cause of Chinese people's dislike of Japan and Japanese people is the actions of the Japanese in Manchuria. The effort to boycott Japanese goods is the real difficulty that troubles and frightens Japan, but as long as the reason for the boycott exists, it will be difficult to weaken it in the end.

Japanese Warships Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon 122

Five Warships Came to Anchor in the Huangpu River

Aircraft from Aircraft Carrier to Arrive This Morning

Since the Japanese conflict incident on North Sichuan Road occurred, the Japanese Navy Ministry has dispatched a large number of warships to Shanghai. This matter has already been

Page 14

reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, around 3:00 PM, Japanese warships began to arrive in Shanghai one after another, and 500 marines were also transported. The aircraft carrier can also arrive in Shanghai this morning. It is reported that there are also fighter planes that are directly loaded from merchant ships. The information obtained by the reporter's investigation is reported as follows:

Destroyers Arrived First The warships dispatched to Shanghai by the Japanese Navy Ministry this time are four second-class destroyers: "Susuki," "Ogi," "Fuji," and "Kuzu." These ships came from Wu Naval Port and Sasebo. They were originally scheduled to enter the port yesterday morning, but due to fog on the sea, they were delayed until 3:15 PM yesterday afternoon before entering the Huangpu River. Commander Shiozawa of the Shanghai First Overseas Dispatch Fleet received the telegram early. Therefore, when the ships entered the port, he ordered them to be anchored in the Yangshupu River to await dispatch.

Cruiser Arrived Later The cruiser "Oi," which commanded the 15th Squadron's four destroyers, also departed from Wu Naval Port at the same time. However, because it was carrying a large number of 500 marines and the soldiers' ammunition, it was delayed until 3:30 PM yesterday afternoon before it was able to enter Wusong. Only because there were marines on board who had to disembark on land, when "Oi" arrived in Shanghai, it was ordered to dock at the Huishan Wharf.

Aircraft Carrier To Arrive Soon The aircraft carrier "Notoro" was originally dispatched to the Lushun area. It has now been reassigned to Shanghai. The aircraft carrier telegraphed Shanghai yesterday, saying that it had loaded a squadron of aircraft in Lushun on the 21st and was heading south, and was expected to arrive in Shanghai at 8:00 AM today. The ship will first stop outside the mouth of Wusong.

Ten Warships Stationed in Shanghai The original Japanese warships stationed in Shanghai, "Ataka," "Hirado," "Tokiwa," and "Urakaze," are under the command of the First Overseas Dispatch Fleet. Now, a cruiser, an aircraft carrier, and four destroyers have been added, totaling ten ships. The Japanese Navy Ministry telegraphed that all ships arriving in Shanghai would be under the command of Rear Admiral Shiozawa. Yesterday, after the "Oi" and other ships arrived in Shanghai, Commander Shiozawa met with the captains of each ship to discuss their tasks. In the afternoon, he also sent marines to patrol the North Sichuan Road area. The soldiers, in rows of six or seven, or more than ten, were all wearing red cloth armbands on both sides of the Target Road, with our armed police seriously maintaining law and order.

Japan's Trade with China Last Year 123

Both Exports and Imports Decreased

According to a telegram from Tokyo received by the Japanese Commercial Counselor's Office in Shanghai, in 1931, Japan's foreign trade (including colonies) totaled 117.9 million yuan in exports and 131.8 million yuan in imports, a decrease of 22% in exports and 21% in imports compared to the previous year. That year, trade with China totaled 25.8 million yuan in exports and the total value of imports was 2.1 million yuan less than the total value of exports, a decrease of 16% in imports and 36% in exports compared to the previous year.

Central Government Loan Successful 124

Shanghai Financial Community to Undertake 8 Million

Financial Committee to be Established on a Regular Basis

The Huadong News Agency reports that the central government has repeatedly consulted with the Shanghai financial community to raise loans due to financial difficulties. This matter has been repeatedly contacted and is close to completion. Minister of Finance Huang Hanliang came to Shanghai a few days ago to further consult with the Shanghai financial community. The consultation has been successful in general. The reporter from the Huadong News Agency visited yesterday and learned that the loan has been completely successful, with the total amount determined to be 8 million yuan. The Bank of China and the Bank of Communications will bear 4 million yuan, other banks will bear 2 million yuan, the money industry will bear 1 million yuan, and the exchange will bear 1 million yuan. The payment can be made within days. Huang will also return to Beijing tomorrow night. Regarding the organization of the Finance Committee, the Ministry of Finance has been actively proceeding and will be established in days. The location has been determined to be within the office of the Ministry of Finance, and internal personnel have begun working.

Three Orders from the Ministry of Finance Arrive in Shanghai 125

Consolidate the Credit of Public Bonds

Sun Ke, President of the Executive Yuan, sent a telegram to Ma Dianzhong of the Six Public Groups in this city on the 21st of this month, stating, "The government is deeply sympathetic to consolidating bond credit and has ordered the Ministry of Finance to order the Customs and Salt Tax Administration and the Chief Inspectorate of Customs to handle it diligently." It was heard yesterday that the Ministry of Finance has issued three orders based on the order of the Executive Yuan, to the Customs and Salt Tax Administration and the Chief Inspectorate of Customs. The contents of the orders are recorded below:

Order to the Chief Inspectorate of Customs to comply. It is hereby ordered that the various internal debts guaranteed by customs duties, including the ㈠ Seventh Year Six Percent Public Bonds, ㈡ Reorganization Six Percent Public Bonds, ㈢ Reorganization Seven Percent Public Bonds, and ㈣ Fourteenth Year Public Bonds issued by the old Beijing government, are all kept in the Internal Debt Fund Office of the Chief Inspectorate of Customs. The ㈠ Reissuance of the Jianghai Customs 25% Additional Tax Treasury Bills, ㈡ Post-Rehabilitation Short-Term Public Bonds, ㈢ Seventeenth Year Financial Short-Term Public Bonds, ㈣ Seventeenth Year Financial Long-Term Public Bonds, ㈤ Disaster Relief Public Bonds, ㈥ Eighteenth Year Disarmament Public Bonds, ㈦ Eighteenth Year Customs Treasury Bills, ㈧ Eighteenth Year Disbandment Treasury Bills, ㈨ Nineteenth Year Customs Public Bonds, ㈩ Nineteenth Year Customs Treasury Bills, ㈩㈠ Nineteenth Year Post-Rehabilitation Treasury Bills, ㈩㈡ Twentieth Year Customs Treasury Bills, and ㈩㈢ Twentieth Year Financial Short-Term Public Bonds issued by the National Government, a total of thirteen funds, are all allocated monthly by the Chief Inspectorate of Customs to the Jianghai Customs 25% Treasury Bills Fund Management Committee for safekeeping, and are used to pay the principal and interest. It has been ordered to comply with this in the record. Now, the Ministry hereby solemnly declares that all of the above public bond treasury bill principal and interest funds should be the responsibility of the Chief Inspectorate of Customs to absolutely comply with the previous decisions and various regulations, and the funds kept by the Chief Inspectorate of Customs should be deposited and paid on schedule. The funds kept by the Jianghai Customs 25% Additional Tax Treasury Bills Fund Management Committee should be allocated in full on schedule until the principal and interest are fully paid. Before it is fully paid, no delay, shortage, or change should be made for any reason. In addition, the Jianghai Customs 25% Additional Tax Treasury Bills Fund Management Committee should be informed of this matter on the date of receipt of the order. This order.

Order to the General Office of Salt Affairs Inspection to comply. It is hereby ordered that the Twentieth Year Disaster Relief Public Bond Regulations and the Twentieth Year Salt Tax Treasury Bill Regulations both designate the salt tax as the principal and interest repayment fund, which is allocated monthly by the Office to the Jianghai Customs 25% Additional Tax Treasury Bills Fund Management Committee for safekeeping. It has been ordered to comply with this in the record. Now, the Ministry hereby solemnly declares that all of the above two public bond treasury bill funds should be absolutely complied with in accordance with the regulations and decisions by the Office, and should be allocated monthly in full to the Jianghai Customs 25% Additional Tax Treasury Bills Fund Management Committee for safekeeping until the principal and interest are repaid. Before it is repaid, no shortage, delay, or change should be made for any reason. In addition, the Jianghai Customs 25% Additional Tax Treasury Bills Fund Management Committee should be notified of this matter on the date of receipt of the order. This order.

Order to the Tax Administration to comply. It is hereby ordered that the Regulations for the Reissuance of Tobacco Tax Treasury Bills, the Nineteenth Year Tobacco Treasury Bill Regulations, the Twentieth Year Tobacco Treasury Bill Regulations, and the Unified Tax Treasury Bill Regulations all designate the tobacco and other unified taxes as the principal and interest repayment fund, which is allocated monthly by the Administration to the Jianghai Customs 25% Additional Tax Treasury Bills Fund Management Committee for safekeeping. It has been ordered to comply with this in the record. Now, the Ministry hereby solemnly declares that all of the above four treasury bill funds should be absolutely complied with in accordance with the regulations and decisions by the Administration, and should be allocated monthly in full to the Treasury Bill Fund Management Committee for safekeeping until the principal and interest are repaid. Before it is repaid, no shortage, delay, or change should be made for any reason. In addition, the Fund Management Committee should be notified of this matter on the date of receipt of the order. This order (January 23, 21st year).

Japan to Blockade Yarn Factories in China 126

Tokyo, 23rd, Electric Communication Agency - The Spinning Industry Association in China convened a committee at 1:00 PM today and received a report from the Osaka Shipping Industry Association on the anti-Japanese situation. After various parties presented their opinions and negotiated countermeasures, they concluded that due to the changing situation, 50-60% of the spinning products in China were in stock and sales had completely stagnated, resulting in various financial difficulties. Although operations have been scaled back, it is difficult to maintain them. Therefore, when it is unavoidable, all spinning factories in Shanghai will be completely closed down.

Local News Two

Xiong Bingsan's Speech on Child Welfare 128

Five Great Hopes

May the People of the Nation Unanimously Support Them

The Chinese Child Welfare Association recently welcomed Mr. Xiong Bingsan. The following is a transcript of his speech:

(Above omitted) I, Xiling, have served society for fifteen or sixteen years. In the past, I lived a political life, too far removed from the common people, and did not know what was meant by the suffering of the people. Since handling a flood disaster in the fifth year of the Republic, I personally went down to investigate and only then did I understand the conditions of rural life and the past mistakes and sins of our political circles. I became indifferent to politics and resolutely put it aside, focusing on strength and social service. I thought that the people are the foundation of the country, and children are the foundation of the people. Moreover, those who have already grown up are fixed in their ways, whether good or bad, and cannot be improved. Only children are like a large, uncarved jade, a blank sheet of paper that has not been stained. As long as we put in some effort and teach them well, everyone can become a healthy citizen. This is such an important issue! So I started from this point. Taking advantage of the fact that there was a child welfare bureau in Peiping in the past, I took in disaster-stricken children in the disaster area. Over time, more and more were taken in, reaching over 20,000. The child welfare bureau could not accommodate them, so another place was opened to raise them. However, they only had food and clothing. After a few months, the disaster situation subsided, and their parents gradually came to take them home. There were still one or two thousand orphans without parents or support, and no one to claim them. Only then was the Xiangshan Child Welfare Institute established. After several years of operation, there were no results, which worried me greatly. After careful study, I realized that they were doing it as a bureaucratic formality, so it got worse and worse. I personally went down to run several factories and set up several schools. Although they were not very good, I was much more confident than before. It was only because of my research in recent years and the problems that arose with our institute that I gathered with you charitable people today. I have five hopes. The first is to unify the national child welfare organizations, sharing strengths and complementing weaknesses. We who run charitable undertakings all face economic difficulties. Even those who do not face economic difficulties find it difficult to do everything in the world well. For example, in our child welfare, all young children should be cared for. If the child is healthy and intelligent, there is naturally no problem. However, if we encounter disabled children (blind, deaf, mute, lame, or with congenital syphilis or lung disease or leprosy) or children with bad character, if we take them in, it will harm the majority of children. If we do not take them in, they will die of illness or commit crimes. This is greatly contrary to our child welfare principles. What can we do to remedy this? We must establish schools for blind children and various institutions for the disabled, as well as various specialized hospitals, to accommodate disabled children. We must establish reformatories and educational institutions to accommodate children with bad character. May I ask, can one organization do all these things? Therefore, I hope that the Chinese Child Welfare Association will take on this responsibility, unite all the national child welfare organizations and charitable organizations. When encountering the above-mentioned children, they should be sent to the respective specialized organizations for care. In this way, there will be no abandoned children, and we can answer to our conscience in child welfare. This is the first hope.

The second is to use new scientific knowledge to improve China's early childhood education. China's great illnesses are poverty and ignorance. Of course, the poor do not have the opportunity for education, and the rich often do not know the methods of education, either being too strict or too lenient. Or else, they indulge in opium, mahjong, and theater, only knowing how to live the life of the rich, not knowing that they are creating a bad environment for their children. May I ask, are they qualified to talk about education? Some also send their children to school, but only at the primary school age of six or seven. Regardless of the quality of primary school education, early childhood education is simply not mentioned. Moreover, a child's intelligence is greatly related to their physical health. Some children suffer from bedwetting and are extremely dull, disliked by everyone. Later, after their illness was cured, they became smarter day by day. It can be seen that physical health is closely related to intelligence, and children not getting proper recreation will also hinder their physical health. These are all things that I have recently investigated. I know deeply that the Chinese Child Welfare Association focuses on children's education, not just on rescuing poor children, but also on carefully studying the educational methods for rich children. Therefore, I hope that the Chinese Child Welfare Association will take on this responsibility, unite specialized child welfare talents, and use new scientific knowledge to improve this early childhood education. This is my second hope.

The third is to establish nanny schools to train specialized child welfare personnel. There used to be a saying in China that one should learn how to raise a child before marrying. It can be seen that we Chinese do not pay attention to the way to nurture children. Once we have children, we simply follow what others say and let them grow up on their own. The poor need not be mentioned. Just talking about the rich, as soon as they have a child, they hire a wet nurse, not knowing that the wet nurse is always making things difficult for the employer, often threatening to quit. Does she have the knowledge to raise children? It is just that there is a lack of such talent, so they have to make do. I plan to set up a kindergarten, and there are two problems. One is the age requirement. The children in the kindergarten start at the age of four. However, the four-year-old children who are taken in are all malnourished and cannot attend classes. We must first raise their bodies before we can talk about it. After they are raised well, it will take at least a year and a half, which exceeds the age limit. To solve this problem, we must also set up a Montessori school, taking in children from two or three years old, and first putting them in the Montessori school to condition their bodies. After they are raised well, they can attend kindergarten classes. This does not delay their time. The other problem is the nanny. If we set up a Montessori school, we must have a nanny. However, there is no such talent in the old society, and the new scholars have not trained this specialist. What can we do? So I called my daughter to Columbia University in the United States to specialize in child welfare issues. Distant water cannot quench immediate thirst, so I did an experiment and set up a nanny class to cultivate specialized talents, and set up a Montessori school and a kindergarten, each one, as a place for practical practice to temporarily take in young children. Their families are all very good, because of various problems, they cannot maintain their current living conditions, and many of their mothers are educated. I thought of a way to take in their children and called their mothers to be nannies, giving them wages as appropriate, for a period of one year. Sometimes I call the students in the training class to serve and practice, freeing up her body to train in the class. If there are more of these talents, they can be assigned to various places to serve. I hope that the Chinese Child Welfare Association will take on this responsibility, find specialized nanny talents, research specialized methods for teaching and educating young children, and contribute to society. This is my third hope.

(Right) Mr. Wu Weide, Director-General of the Chinese Child Welfare Association

(Middle) Mr. Xiong Xiling

(Left) Dr. Hu Xuanming, Executive Committee Member of the Chinese Child Welfare Association. The fourth is to convene a national child welfare conference every year. It is not that things are difficult to handle, but that talent is hard to come by. It is not that there are no truly noble specialized talents, but that it is really because of economic difficulties that we cannot afford to hire them. For example, my Xiangshan Child Welfare Institute used to focus on crafts, so we opened several factories, allowing them to learn crafts according to their interests. But we must give them a general knowledge, so we opened several classes of schools, with primary, senior primary, and junior high school levels. Later, we saw that they were very excellent and could not be buried, so we opened a senior high school level for them to go to college. Later, we saw that the graduating students had very good results and should go to university. We were limited by economic reality and could not afford to open it, and we could not bear to hinder their progress, so we discussed with the Xiangshan Agricultural and Industrial Bank, asking them to lend money to the students for university expenses, providing them with a university degree, and the compensation they received after graduation must be excellent, and then repay the principal. This method does not lose money for the bank, and the students are not wronged. There are already several who have entered university. However, running a class of schools, no matter how many students there are, hiring teachers, opening classrooms, and purchasing all educational supplies, are all indispensable. Calculating it, there must be two classes of junior high school for a class of senior high school, and two classes of senior primary school for a class of junior high school to be able to go to school. Our institute often has students who are not enough to advance to the next grade. Previously, the Chinese Child Welfare Association sent ten students, and now their level is very good. If the national child welfare organizations can unite, sending the students of this school to that school can save the difficulty of opening classes and avoid the situation of vacancies, and can also exchange knowledge. In the future, the child welfare cause will naturally flourish. We plan to imitate the methods of the National Chamber of Commerce and the National Education Association, convene a national conference, and hold it in various places in turn, which can be used to investigate the child welfare organizations in each place and mutually seek improvement. This is my fourth hope.

The fifth is to arouse social sympathy and attract public attention. Last year, the Chinese Child Welfare Association submitted a request to the National Government to approve April 4th as Children's Day, and the Ministry of Education issued a notice to all schools to hold celebrations. This year, on April 4th, celebrations should be held to expand publicity. But this publicity has two meanings. One is to let the social public understand the importance of the child welfare cause, and everyone should rise up, focus on studying how to teach and how to raise children, and give practical support to us. The other is to imitate the method of the American Golden Rule Day (on the American Golden Rule Day, donations are made for poor children all over the country, also known as Children's Happiness Day). We can imitate this and ask all the charitable people in the country to do their best to donate and contribute to this righteous cause. This is my fifth hope. (Below omitted)

Invention of Vacuum Milk Condensing Machine 129

"Swallow" Brand Condensed Milk to be Marketed in Shanghai

Mr. Xiao Jiagan, a former teacher at Zhejiang Provincial Senior High School, and Mr. Xu Kangzu, a technician at the Zhejiang Construction Department, spent two and a half years inventing a vacuum milk condensing machine. Its special feature is that the condenser in the machine is specially purchased and is different from those manufactured in various countries. It can completely extract the fishy smell from the milk, so the condensed milk produced has a very fresh taste and no fishy smell. The vacuum milk condensing machine is a single-effect type, first created by the American Gail Borden in 1853. Since then, the condensed milk industry has flourished and the demand has increased day by day. Although our country has a great need, there are no factories or machines to manufacture it, and the benefits flow out, exceeding five million yuan per year. Recently, Messrs. Xiao and Zhang Xiongfei have raised funds to establish the West Lake Condensed Milk Co., Ltd. The factory is located outside Qiantang Gate in Hangzhou, and the cattle farm is located in Xiyancang, Haining County, with more than 1,000 acres of pasture and 200 dairy cows. It is said that since the product was launched, it has been well received by the society, especially in the counties of Hangzhou, Jiaxing, and Huzhou. Recently, Messrs. Yu and Tang organized Shenchang Huahang to manage the company's "Swallow" brand condensed milk and market it in Shanghai. It is said that major pharmacies, Guanshengyuan, and other food merchants and stores all sell it.

Since the promulgation of the Provisional Regulations for Physicians and Pharmacists and the Regulations for Midwives, physicians, pharmacists, and midwives in this city have successively applied to the Municipal Health Bureau for forwarding to the Ministry of Health of the Interior to obtain licenses. Clock and Watch Industry Requests Reduction of Tax Rate 134

It is reported that more than 80 companies in the city's clock and watch industry, including Huade, Meihuali, Hengdali, Hengdeli, Maodeli, Zhongmei, Shichangtai, and Huaxingli, jointly requested the industry association to request the Jianghai Customs authorities to revise and reduce the tax rate because the customs tax rate is too heavy and difficult to bear. The association held a meeting and decided to submit a tax rate to the Jianghai Customs authorities for approval, classified by category: (1) 40% for gold inlaid with real diamonds; (2) 15% for yellow and white gold and inlaid with imitation diamonds; (3) 12% for silver-plated gold, gold-plated nickel, iron, etc. The case has been recorded and submitted to the Jianghai Customs Superintendent for quick verification and reduction and early implementation.

Farmers Fear Thieves Binding Their Son, Pointing Out the Location of Hidden Silver 135

His Wife Was Unwilling and Shouted "Thieves!"

Shot in the Right Thigh by Thieves

Zhou Fugen, a 58-year-old local farmer living in a bungalow in Zhou's house, Panxin Road, Avenue Joffre, French Concession, and his wife, Yuan, 44 years old, started their business through diligence and thrift and had a little property, which attracted the covetousness of bandits. At 7:30 last night, eight bandits suddenly came, three of whom were armed with pistols, threatening and intimidating the victim. At first, Zhou said he had no money and begged for forgiveness, but the bandits did not believe him and tried to kidnap his son. Zhou was extremely frightened and immediately pointed out the location of the hidden silver. All gold and silver jewelry, clothing, and other items, estimated to be worth about 3,000 yuan, and a deed, worth about 6,000 taels of land, were looted after ransacking the boxes. When the bandits were about to leave, Yuan was unwilling and shouted "Thieves!" repeatedly. Fearing that the patrolmen would hear the alarm, one bandit turned back and fired a shot, hitting Yuan's right thigh. The bullet went through, and blood flowed like a stream. The bandits then swaggered away. Later, someone reported to patrolman No. 236, who arrived at the scene, but the bandits had already left. They had to send the injured woman to Renji Hospital for treatment. The victim Zhou Fugen issued a loss report and reported to the Shanzhong Road Police Station for arrest.

A Russian Man, Fearing Western Detectives, Commits Suicide by Taking Poison 136

Dies a Tragic Death

A Russian man, Hui Ersheng, 40 years old, opened a musical instrument store at No. 429 Jing'an Temple Road. At about 4 p.m. the day before yesterday, Western detective Biesalesun from the Xinzha Police Station and another Westerner went to the store to investigate debt matters. At that time, when Hui Ersheng saw the detectives coming, he said to his wife, "The police are here to arrest me!" and ordered the Western detectives to enter through the back door. Then he turned around and took poison himself, and there was an empty bottle of medicine on his table. When his wife came forward to ask, Hui said goodbye to his wife, and then became dizzy. The Western detectives sent him to Baolong Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he died shortly after. The body was taken to the Fei Lun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, prosecutor of the First Special District Court, and forensic doctor Wei Ligong and clerk Liu Zhuang arrived at the morgue to examine the body. According to the wife's statement, Guo determined that the deceased, Russian Hui Ersheng, had died of poisoning. The body was handed over to his wife to collect the coffin for burial after signing a guarantee.

Accepting the Manufacturing of Garbage Cans for the Entire French Concession 137

A Case of Fraudulent Acquisition of Property by Issuing Bad Checks Occurs

Wu Shaowu yesterday extended to Lawyers Xichang and Huang Han as agents, prosecuted Zhu Kongyang, the owner of the Fuyu Company, in the Second Special District Court for issuing bad checks, frauding property, requesting legal punishment, and incidental civil lawsuit. It is briefly stated that the defendant falsely claimed on August 26 of last year that he had received an order from the French Municipal Council and the French Consul General to handle the garbage cans for the entire French Concession, and entrusted the plaintiff to contract for the manufacture of iron cans, setting up a contract where each can would cost three yuan and two corners of foreign currency, and the delivery time was limited. The defendant also borrowed 1,000 yuan of foreign currency from the plaintiff on November 11 of the same year in the name of establishing the company, with a loan note as proof. The plaintiff believed it was true and delivered 3,132 iron cans, costing 10,022 yuan and four corners of foreign currency, receiving only 2,446 yuan in cash, with a net debt of 7,576 yuan and four corners of foreign currency. The defendant issued two checks dated October 27 and November 3, totaling 2,000 yuan of foreign currency. Upon expiration, there was no money to collect. Because of the contractual relationship, the plaintiff continued to manufacture iron cans, with 3,800 iron cans currently in stock, valued at 8,960 yuan of foreign currency. This item of iron cans is a special commodity, which cannot be used for other purposes and is virtually useless. The defendant defrauded people into believing the fraud and took property. The defendant's fraud of issuing bad checks and violating Article 136 of the Bill Law. Therefore, the plaintiff is requesting legal punishment and recovering 17,536 yuan and four corners of foreign currency. The defendant Zhu Kongyang admitted that it was because the company was attacked and there was no money to pay for a while. All the money collected was deposited in the bank and there was evidence to prove it. He requested a postponement to submit the evidence. Judge Wu instructed Zhu to pay 10,000 yuan in silver and be released on bail to await continued interrogation on the adjourned date.

Public Works Bureau Reorganizes Public Docks 139

Managed Concurrently by the Dock Warehouse Management Office

In addition to the docks leased by shipping companies and those dedicated to various industries, there are many public docks along the Huangpu River and Wusong River in the city, which have been used arbitrarily by merchants and people without a dedicated management agency. The Municipal Government, in view of the disorderly loading and unloading of goods at these public docks, deemed it necessary to reorganize them and submitted a proposal to the Municipal Council, which was resolved and handed over to the Public Works Bureau for management. It is now known that the bureau has assigned the management of public dock affairs to the Dock Warehouse Management Office. Citizens can contact the office at the mouth of Maojia Lane, Wai Ma Lu, for matters related to public docks.

Extortionists Armed with Guns Extort at Foreman's Home 140

Fifty Dollars and a Coat Demanded

Repeated Telephone Calls to Demand Remaining Money

Police Arrest Three Suspects

Yu Zhengmou, a Taixing native residing at No. 14 Baoding Road and employed as a foreman at the Shanghai Electric Power Company, received a threatening letter from a criminal gang between the 9th and 18th of this month, demanding 1,000 dollars. He reported the matter to the Huishan Police Station. The police chief ordered detectives Qi Mengqing and Cai Zhitian to arrest Xu Jinshan, a Jiangbei native, at the Wuhua Yang Bottle Factory at No. 276 South Chengdu Road on the afternoon of the day before yesterday. Xu confessed that his accomplice was Chen Hengtai (also from Jiangbei), who lived at No. 1224 Datong Road. The detectives secretly went to arrest Chen and also took a suspected Jiangbei woman, Wu Chen, into custody. They were detained separately and escorted to the First Special Court, High Division One, the next morning. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's lawyer, stated that the case involved three criminals who suddenly arrived at the home of the plaintiff, Yu Zhengmou, around 6 p.m. on the 9th of this month. One of them had a gun and, under the pretext of discussing the termination of workers with Yu, claimed that the dismissed workers planned to take drastic measures, posing a threat to Yu's life, and demanded 1,000 dollars to settle the matter. Seeing the menacing attitude of the group, Yu agreed to give them 50 dollars as a mediation fee and handed over the money. As they left, the group forcibly took Yu's coat and fled. Around 1 p.m. on the 14th, Yu received two threatening letters by mail, instructing him to negotiate at the Changle Tea House on Fuzhou Road at 6 p.m. on the 16th. He went as agreed, but no one came to meet him. At 2 p.m. on the 18th, he received another letter signed "Song," as well as two phone calls urging him to pay the money. One call came from Apartment No. 9 on Jing'an Temple Road, which was found to be a telephone installed by a German named Kao Laotuo, but the location of the German's office could not be determined. The other call came from No. 276 South Chengdu Road, which was found to be the location of the Wuhua Glass Factory. The detectives rushed to the factory to investigate and found Xu Jinshan about to make another call to urge payment. They arrested him and, after interrogation, learned of Chen's whereabouts. They went with Xu to identify and arrest Chen and also learned that the mastermind behind the case was Wu Ruizhi, Chen's "old man," and that Wu Chen was his wife, so she was also arrested. Xu confessed at the police station that five people went to the plaintiff's house on the 9th of this month. Yu's coat has been recovered from the Xinfeng Pawnshop at No. 618 Xinzha Road. The case is requested to be adjourned for further investigation. The coat and threatening letters were presented as evidence. The plaintiff, Yu Zhengmou, submitted a report stating that on the afternoon of the 9th, he saw Xu Jinshan enter first, followed by Chen Hengtai, an unfamiliar criminal with a gun, who stood by the escalator. They told Yu that the matter could not be settled for less than 1,000 dollars, or the lives of Yu and his son would be at risk. When Yu pleaded for a reduction, they said the lowest amount was 500 dollars. Fearing a shooting, Yu agreed to pay 50 dollars first, and Chen Hengtai accompanied Yu's wife upstairs to collect the money. As they left, they snatched Yu's coat and left. The original stolen goods are presented. After questioning the defendants, Judge Shen Bingrong ordered them to be remanded in custody for further investigation at a later date. The coat was returned to its owner.

Laborer Crushed to Death by Large Iron Bucket 141

At the Zhengtai Rubber Overshoe Factory at the intersection of Dalian Bay Road and Kunming Road in Hongkou at 10:30 yesterday morning, a large iron bucket, weighing about 500 to 600 pounds, was being lifted by a wooden frame when it suddenly slipped off the hook and fell, crushing the head of a young laborer named A Mao. His brains splattered, and he died on the spot. The Huishan Police Station and a fire truck transported the body to Tongren Hospital and then to the coroner's office for an autopsy.

Outrage of All Circles Over Japanese Riot 146

Declaration of the Municipal Party Headquarters The Municipal Party Headquarters issued a declaration on the Japanese mob riot, stating: This time, Japanese rioters set fire to our Eryou Towel Factory, destroyed our stores along North Sichuan Road, and even destroyed police kiosks and injured police officers. If the Shanghai Chinese and foreign authorities do not impose severe sanctions and allow them to run rampant, then the riot on the 20th is just the beginning. If the Chinese and foreign authorities truly want to maintain local peace and order, they must not take the Japanese atrocities lightly as an occasional incident, but should be deeply vigilant and prevent the recurrence of the Tianjin incident in Shanghai. If the Japanese are given another opportunity to sabotage, then the suffering we will endure will be even greater than in Tianjin, and the impact will not only be on the Chinese side, but also on the foreign residents and the Sino-foreign trade of tens of millions of dollars, which will also suffer. Therefore, for the common interests of China and the world, we sincerely hope that the Shanghai Chinese and foreign authorities will actively work together to find the most effective means of restraint. Anti-Japanese national salvation is our only way out today. No matter what the situation, we must persevere. All our comrades and compatriots should rise up and fight to the death to eradicate the violent Japan that disrupts world peace. This declaration is hereby made for your information.

County Party Headquarters The Shanghai County Party Headquarters and the County Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association submitted a report to the Central Government on this case, stating: On the 20th of this month, Japanese residents set fire to the Eryou Industrial Cooperative Factory, killed and injured many Chinese police officers of the First Special District Municipal Council, and destroyed countless stores along North Sichuan Road. This Association has witnessed and heard of this and is deeply saddened. Since the September 18th Incident, Tianjin, Fuzhou, Guangzhou, Wuhan, and other places have successively been harassed by the Japanese. Their intention is clearly to deliberately provoke trouble, but our government has ultimately failed to provide adequate protection and has tolerated the situation, leading to the huge disaster of factory burning and murder. Moreover, this incident occurred within the concession area protected by foreigners, so it is difficult to escape unscathed, let alone other areas. This Association hates the barbarity of the Japanese and mourns the humiliation of the Chinese people. As long as the Japanese are in our territory, the Chinese people will not have peace. Therefore, we hereby request your Association to immediately declare the severance of diplomatic relations with Japan and order Japanese residents to leave the country to prevent future troubles and protect the people. This is for the convenience of the Party.

Declaration of the Shanghai Municipal Local Self-Government Promotion Association 150

Third Preparatory Meeting Held Yesterday

The Shanghai Municipal Local Self-Government Promotion Association held its third preparatory meeting yesterday. Wang Binyan, Ling Zhibin, Chen Yafu, Yang Xinzheng, and other seven people attended. The following four items were resolved: 1. The revised articles of association were approved; 2. Joining the National Local Self-Government Promotion Association and sending personnel to negotiate; 3. Designating the Zhabei Chamber of Commerce as the association's address; 4. The association's declaration was revised and approved for publication. The declaration is as follows: Shanghai is the key transportation hub of the Yangtze River and the sea, and the meeting place of Chinese and foreigners. Cultural exchange is constant, and the people are educated. The cause of local self-government was already roughly established in the late Qing Dynasty. After the promulgation of the municipal and township systems in the early Republic of China, people of insight struggled to manage it, and there were considerable achievements. Although the people's administration was destroyed and replaced by official administration, the local people were still able to supervise the government and assist in the process, thereby achieving results. For example, in road construction, the construction of Xuxu Road and Xietu Road in southern Shanghai, the construction of Jungong Road, Songhu Road, and Xiangyin Road in northern Shanghai, and the construction of the Tanggong Bureau Road in Pudong, and the planning of various roads by the Transportation Bureau in Baoshan, are all visible to the eye. Other undertakings also have prototypes. When self-government was restored in June of the twelfth year of the Republic of China, public opinion was revived and people's administration became more prominent. In short, allowing local people to handle local affairs prevents public sentiment from being blocked, and designs are easily promoted. This is the clear and effective verification of this. However, the world is constantly progressing, and nothing can be perfected without changing. Shanghai and Baoshan are located adjacent to each other, and only by working together can we achieve twice the result with half the effort. If the city and townships each govern their own affairs, the situation will be narrow and the financial resources will be weak, how can we compete with the prosperous concession? Therefore, the demand to establish the Songhu Special Municipality has been rising in the newspapers, and people of insight should be able to recall it. The result of the appeal was only the establishment of the Songhu Municipal Administration Office, which did not fully meet the expectations of the people. In the spring of the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, the National Revolutionary Army arrived in Shanghai. In July of the same year, the city-county zoning was determined. In June of the following year, the original seventeen municipalities and townships in Shanghai were merged under the jurisdiction of the Municipal Government and municipal commissioners were appointed to assist in governance. The people of Shanghai yearned for proper governance, believing that their wishes could be fulfilled. In the future, actively developing construction and opening up port affairs could complete the plan of General Sun Yat-sen's Great Shanghai. However, in recent years, internal strife has not ceased, and municipal administration has been affected by it. Public opinion has not been expressed, and there are still obstacles, which is an undeniable fact that the people of Shanghai have heard and seen. Now that the political system has been reformed to jointly relieve the national crisis, the government allows the people freedom of assembly, association, speech, and publication. Therefore, the repressed public sentiment of several years has been fully expressed at once, and mass organizations are emerging like a rising wind and clouds. This is truly a good phenomenon in the era of preparing for constitutional government, which the government should praise and maintain. The members of our association were born in Shanghai, grew up in Shanghai, have careers in Shanghai, and their lives depend on Shanghai. Their joys and sorrows are different from those of officials who are only transient. Therefore, based on the heart of loving the country first and loving the hometown, we organized this association so that people from the city and districts can gather together, draft simple regulations, and elect officials, and it was established on a certain day of a certain month. This is to represent the citizens, and this is to promote municipal administration, directly seek the happiness of the entire city, and indirectly promote the observation of proper governance. We hope that the elders, brothers, sisters, and aunts of the entire city will supervise and guide us, so that our association can follow this hope. This declaration is hereby made.

Declarations of the Two Postal Workers' Unions Advocating for the Recovery of the Savings and Remittance Bureau 152

To the public across the country: Since the Ministry of Communications established the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau on March 15th of the 19th year of the Republic [1930], ostensibly to exclusively handle postal savings and remittance services, the postal savings and remittance business has in reality continued to be concurrently handled by designated post offices. Our unions have repeatedly striven with the authorities to merge this kind of deformed, redundant organization that disrupts the postal organization system and wastes public funds, and have also loudly appealed to our compatriots in the hope that they will sympathize and assist us, so that the Chinese postal service, which has been painstakingly managed for over thirty years, will not suffer the disaster of division and destruction. However, time has passed, and two years have elapsed, and our goal has not yet been achieved, but the dangers facing the postal service have become all around us. If the savings and remittance business is not recovered for even one day, not only will the foundation of the postal service be shaken, but also the savings and remittance business, in which the people of the whole country have invested their lifelong hard-earned money, will also face the disaster of collapse due to the lack of separation from politics. At this critical moment, our unions are very vigilant and will certainly uphold their mission and work actively to achieve the original intention of merging the savings and remittance business, and to save the postal service from danger. This can be truthfully told to our compatriots. However, recent political tides have risen and fallen, inevitably affecting the postal service. Therefore, our unions feel even more keenly the importance of the mission we bear, and before this savings and remittance business is merged, there must be emergency remedies. There are three remedies: In order to protect the interests of the public's savings and to guarantee the credit of the postal savings and remittance business, all accounts of the Savings and Remittance General Bureau must be audited jointly by the representatives of the staff and workers, and published in detail, and all assets, securities, funds, and accounts must be kept in the custody of the joint accounting office of the Savings and Remittance General Bureau and the Postal General Bureau, and must not be appropriated or used, so as to avoid unexpected catastrophes, which is an urgent and indispensable plan. This is the first. All personnel of the Savings and Remittance General Bureau, from the deputy director downwards, must be filled by postal personnel, and all current personnel who are not from the postal service must be tested, and those who pass will continue to be retained, otherwise they will be dismissed, and it must be strictly stipulated that no officials who have not been tested shall be employed in the future. In this way, the postal examination system will not be destroyed, and the abuses of recommendation and filling of positions will be prevented. This is the second. The postal economy should prioritize the development of the postal service, which is still insufficient, such as the restoration of postal lines, the expansion of bureaus and offices, which are all related to the interests of the people. If this is not done, and all resources are wasted on unnecessary undertakings, there is a reversal of priorities. Since the country has suffered from wars for years and has also been hit by disasters, the postal income has been greatly reduced. If the marrow is squeezed out and used for other purposes, it is unlikely that it will not collapse. Therefore, there should be clear regulations on the postal economy, prioritizing the development of the postal service. This is the third. All three of these are emergency measures to recover the Savings and Remittance General Bureau. Our unions vow to fight to the death and never change our minds, and will not hesitate to make any sacrifices. We dare to tell the people of the country everything we know, and hope that compatriots from all walks of life across the country will rise up together to uphold the safety of the postal service and the savings and remittance business, which truly depends on it. This declaration is hereby made on January 23rd of the 21st year of the Republic of China.

Merchants' Bureau Staff Telegraph Request to Retain Guo 153

The staff of the General and Branch Bureaus of the Merchants' Bureau telegraphed the government, saying: To Chairman Lin of the Nanjing National Government, President Sun of the Executive Yuan, and Vice President Chen, The Merchants' Bureau is the largest shipping institution in our country. In the past, due to the influence of the political situation and the improper management, it was heavily indebted and at a loss. The current Commissioner of the General Administration Office, Guo Waifeng, was appointed at a time when various shipping companies were required to dispatch soldiers and there was no income at all. The situation was extremely difficult. Commissioner Guo, amid all the difficulties, made appropriate arrangements, maintaining the original living conditions of the staff and workers, and also purchasing two more ocean liners, so that the shipping industry had a momentum of advancing a thousand miles a day. His talent and knowledge are outstanding, and his reorganization is well-organized, truly opening a new era for the Merchants' Bureau. With such talent in the country, the future of shipping administration will surely shine brightly. However, we have heard that Commissioner Guo, because the crew members of various ships requested to be paid double wages, suddenly had the intention to resign and requested to resign. Upon hearing this, the public was bewildered. We think that the Bureau's finances are in a desperate situation, and fortunately, thanks to Commissioner Guo's reorganization, there has been a gradual improvement. We sincerely request that you look into the situation and grant him comfort and retention, so that the lives of thousands of staff and workers will not be affected. The Merchants' Bureau will be very fortunate, and all the staff and workers will be very fortunate. We are in great trepidation and cannot express our eagerness to await orders. Western Policeman on Patrol Shot by Bandit 158

Criminal Killed in Thatched Cottage

At 9:15 PM last night, Western policeman Smith No. 133 of the Gordon Road Police Station led detectives on patrol in the Binlang Road area and saw a short-clothed person whose behavior was suspicious. He ordered him to stop, but the person continued to move forward. The Western policeman was anxious and chased him. In an instant, the person shot at the Western policeman with a pistol, and the bullet injured the Western policeman's lower jaw. The policeman also returned fire but missed and was escaped by him without a trace. At that time, a nearby sentry heard the gunshots and urgently telegraphed the Gordon Road Police Station to report the alarm. Three more detectives were dispatched to the scene of the incident, and together with the injured Western policeman, they searched for the criminal in the nearby thatched cottages. Suddenly, a pistol was found in the seam of a thatched cottage, and it was about to be fired outwards. The detectives fired into the house first and killed the criminal on the spot. A pistol was also found on the ground in the house. The injured Western policeman was only grazed by the bullet and was not seriously injured.

The First Production of Mingxing Sida Tong

Other aspects, such as the clarity and pleasingness of the photography and the richness and grandeur of the background, are all excellent. Reader Correspondence

A Letter from a Refugee from the Northeast 165

I am a refugee soldier and student who was shot to Beijing by the foreign guns and cannons of the violent army in this national crisis. Before the September 18th Incident [Mukden Incident], I was studying in the senior high school department of the Northeast Student Team in Shenyang. Because I was condemned by my conscience for being a soldier with a gun who did not take up the gun to fight the violent army and fulfill a little of the military duty of a soldier, I used the money that my family in Suizhong, which had suffered a major flood last year, sent me so that I would no longer live this difficult refugee life and go home, to start a Tie Xue [Iron Blood] Weekly with the purpose of awakening the people, (1) understanding Japan, (2) understanding the Northeast, (3) knowing military affairs, (4) vowing to resist Japan, and (5) saving the country with iron and blood. The first issue was born in this environment. But seven days passed in an instant, and the funds were still not available. After running around for many days, I finally received 10 yuan from our Education Director Wang Yizhe and 94 yuan from General Team Leader Ji Shaoji [the current captain of the 2nd Infantry Team], who persuaded his subordinates to donate, and more than 40 yuan from my own manuscript fees, so that it could continue to be published until the ninth issue, and now it can be said that economic assistance has been cut off. There is no way, so it is in a state of invisible suspension, but I still can't bear to sit idly by and watch this small life sink down like this, so I came up with the idea of asking the comrades in society who are generally passionate, patriotic, and vowed to resist Japan for economic assistance. Although the funds are not much, even small contributions can make a big difference. I hope that comrades from all walks of life will enthusiastically help.

In addition, I also plan to solicit members. All comrades with the same purpose can join the society. Comrades who are enthusiastic, patriotic, vow to resist Japan, and advocate iron and blood for survival are welcome to communicate with Zhang Zuohua, Tie Xue Weekly, No. 13, Jia, Qihe Lou, Beichi Yu, Beijing.

Mr. Zhang, this kind of correspondence is usually not published because of your enthusiasm, we are making an exception to make it public. The methods for joining the society and subscribing to the newspaper are omitted. The Japanese invaders are advancing step by step. I hope people will advocate and hurry up to do practical resistance work. Attached by the reporter.
