Free Talk

Talks from the Thatched Cottage of the Unremoved Weeds

A Lesson on How to Be a Son (Part 2) 166

There is no doubt that a son should be taught to be a son by being a son. If I want every son to become a certain kind of son, I have to become that kind of son myself first. If I want to teach my son to be self-reliant and to help others to be self-reliant, I have to be self-reliant and help others myself. If I want to teach my son to be self-sufficient and to help others to be self-sufficient, I have to be self-sufficient and help others myself. Recently, I and the children discussed a teaching-and-doing process of self-reliance, self-reliance, self-help, and helping others, which is divided into four stages. In the first stage, when three meals are full, everyone shouts "Baby";

In the second stage, small things are done in a small way, and pocket money is earned by oneself;

In the third stage, all food, clothing, shelter, and transportation are not relied on others;

In the fourth stage, there is surplus energy to live independently, and helping others to be self-reliant.

My fourth child is six years old and is still in the first stage. My third child is nine years old. When he was in the countryside, he had already reached the second stage, but now that he has come to the city, he has returned to the first stage. My second child is thirteen years old and is in the second stage. My first child is seventeen years old and is in the third stage. At the same time, everyone is still studying and working together to move forward to the fourth stage.

Chinese society generally has only two stages for the education of children: one is total dependence, and the other is sudden independence. There is a lack of a gradual bridge in between. If adults suddenly encounter changes and children lose their dependence, how painful it is!

Talking about Bai Long with Loyalty and Bravery 167

— Xinfo

Liaoji [Liaoning and Jilin] has fallen. It has been more than a hundred days. The officers guarding the territory did not resist in the front. The responsible government did not send reinforcements in the rear. General Ma could not support the building alone. The common people had nothing to do with their bare hands. Seeing that Shenzhou [China] was about to sink and would no longer belong to me. Therefore, among the black rivers and white waters [Northeast], heroic people rose up and refused bribes to kill the enemy, shocking the enemy's courage, such as Xiao Bailong and Lao Beifeng, who are the most outstanding. A guest from Zhifu [Yantai] told me about Xiao Bailong's defeat of the Japanese army. Hearing this, my blood boiled and I applauded with joy. Hei Ma and Bai Long are also worthy of emulation.

Xiao Bailong's surname is Zhang, and Xing Tian is his given name. He is from Pinggu County, Hebei Province. He was a merchant in his early years and was good at riding, shooting, and dart throwing. He was heroic and righteous, helping the weak and eliminating the strong. He did not pay attention to trading skills. He had three thousand retainers, with the style of Mengchang. In a few years, his family property was gone. Finally, he joined the green forest. However, he still did not change his usual state. He robbed the rich and powerful officials, but helped the poor. In the spring of last year, he was once appeased by the provincial government, but then he became Feng Fu [a hunter who returned to his former profession]. In October of last year, when the Japanese were taking advantage of the protection of the League of Nations and acting wantonly, they wanted to take Jinzhou and station in Tientsin. The Japanese had long heard of Bailong's bravery and secretly bribed him with 10,000 Japanese yuan and hundreds of boxes of artillery, rifles, and bullets to cause trouble. Long pretended to agree and accepted the bribe. The Japanese were overjoyed, thinking that the Chinese were all greedy, and that it would be easy to take the land in one fell swoop. After Long had both money and equipment, he suddenly attacked the Japanese army. Many enemies died. The Japanese were furious and sent troops to retaliate. Long knew that he was no match for them and quickly fled into the mountains and valleys of Tongliao, coming and going quickly and appearing and disappearing unpredictably. The Japanese hated him with gnashing teeth. Now Bailong is planning to contact General Ma and the militia to jointly eliminate the enemy.

Feng Yuxiang's Talk on Politics 168

— Shuilin

Feng's strict military discipline is well known to the Chinese people. His method of purifying politics is also unmatched. Xue Dubi and Guo Zhihuan were Feng's left and right assistants. Xue was in charge of political affairs and Guo was in charge of financial affairs. Both were diligent in politics and firm in integrity, and both were well-known at the time. After Feng settled Henan, the affairs were more troublesome than in the Guannei [inside the pass]. Feng went to the office every morning. Civil and military officials were received in order. If there was any disagreement, he would be punished by beating, kneeling, or facing the wall. It was difficult to avoid it for a day. Not only were officials with small positions like this, but even Xue and Guo, who were respected, could not avoid it. One day, Feng was sitting in the Guang Hall, and Xue was standing to the right, serving. Because he slightly offended his intention, he slapped him in the face and ordered him to redo it immediately. Guo was offended, and it was the same. Afterwards, Xue and Guo did not complain. Feng served in politics and always told people an ancient proverb: "Politics is not about talking more, but about doing it."

Henan's education was less than that of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Feng tried hard to revitalize it. In addition to running the Xunzheng [Political Training] Academy in Kaifeng to train emergency talents, the teachers of each middle school were selected. For a time, the youths of Kyoto [Beijing] and Shanghai with some literary reputation rushed to it like a hundred rivers running into the sea. The youth circles then launched a slogan: "Go to Henan." Its momentum could not be underestimated. This can be seen here. Unfortunately, the war started soon and it was interrupted.

The first National Guoshu [Chinese martial arts] Competition was held at the Nanjing Stadium. On the opening day, various dignitaries came one after another. According to the example, all made speeches. The speech platform was north of the competition platform, and the people were south of the competition platform, more than twenty feet apart. The first few people spoke, and the listeners did not understand very well. They could only see their mouths talking and their fingers gesturing. When Feng spoke, everyone could hear clearly. Speakers said that Feng's speech could be heard by 100,000 people, which was not an exaggeration. The general idea of the speech that day was that today you are here to see, you must learn it in your heart, and you must do it when you go home. It was about two minutes, concise and to the point.

World Anecdotes 169

— Haike

A Hermit Who Never Approached Women in His Lifetime In Birmingham, England, there is an old man named A. Blythwaite, who is 87 years old this year. He claims that he has never approached women in his life and has never kissed a woman. He once said to people, "Since I grew up, after I first knew human affairs, the first step was to strive for independence, without the help of women. When I was fourteen years old, I learned to knit socks for myself and sew buttons on my shirts for myself." At the age of twenty-three, he took care of the housework alone, cooking and washing his own clothes. He also never interacted with women on weekdays. Only once a year did a woman step into his house, and that was when his sister came to visit him on Christmas. Recently, he said to people again, "I am already 87 years old. I am very healthy. I am very happy. I also have money in the bank. The reason why I can be like this is because I have never kissed a woman." But this kind of life is too boring and too uninteresting.

Mud Emperor 170

— Suspicion Begins

Xia Ziyi, a man from the Xiyin Study, is skilled. The Ziyi seal ink he makes is outstanding for its time. For the past year, Xia Zi has been researching and studying the art of making ink, innovating and creating more refined seal inks than before. It can be said that he has truly reached the peak of perfection, meeting the ideal standard. He dares not say there will be none better in the future, but he is undoubtedly the best so far. Xia Ziyi does not easily make ink without good materials. His diligence in searching for them is rare. Last summer, he obtained more than ten catties of four-year-old cinnabar from Hunan. He selected the best, refined it for months, and made several dozen taels of lotus root silk ink. The beauty of its color and quality surpasses even the Xuanhe watermark. The Qianlong Chicheng is even more inferior. The most difficult thing is to make the oil and paste of the ink even and clean. The better the sand, the heavier the quality. The oil should be clear and light. Heavy sinks and light floats are natural laws. Therefore, the best ink, when placed in a jar and not stirred for several days, often has oil floating on top, accumulating around the edges. When stamping on paper, it is easy to create an oily outline. However, if it does not yellow the paper and disappears without a trace over time, it is already extremely refined. As for the inferior quality ink, the oil is originally greasy and stagnant. Even if you want to see the oil floating in the jar, you cannot get it. The ink made by Xia Zi this time, even if it is not stirred for a month, will not have oil floating around. There is no appearance of being thin on top and thick on the bottom. (However, it must be stirred from time to time, so that the ink becomes more and more bright and beautiful, easy to clump together and come out of the jar, which should never be abandoned.) When stamping on paper, there is even less trace of oil to be seen. The refinement of his research, refining, and mixing is unparalleled. Also, purely cinnabar ink is initially dull in color when first made, but gradually becomes glossy, red, and bright over time. The common people often add foreign red and cloud vermilion to speed up the redness, so that it is easy to please the eye when made. However, pure cinnabar ink will be as red and bright as those with foreign red added in one or two years. After a longer period, it will far surpass those with foreign red. It is even more beautiful after being removed from the jar. The color of those mixed with foreign red will fade over time and will never come out of the jar. By examining this, one can understand why pure cinnabar ink is so valuable. Xia Zi makes ink with the intention of passing it down through generations, striving to avoid confusing purple with red and vowing not to mix foreign red vermilion markings. The Ziyi seal ink he makes can provide evidence of being removed from the jar. Therefore, it is completely different from those commonly made. At the beginning of this production, the color and luster were already as bright and red as those stored for two or three years. If it goes through more years, its exquisite beauty will become unimaginable. It will also be easier and faster to remove from the jar than previous productions. The above two points are the greatest advantages of Xia Zi's lotus root silk ink, which surpasses all others. Xia Zi, based on his rich experience and deep research, is able to make it more and more refined. A month ago, this unworthy one sipped tea at the Xiyin Study and had the opportunity to see this newly made product. I praised it as the emperor of ink. Friends who are good at appreciation also said that the evaluation was appropriate. Xia Zi was overjoyed and playfully named his study the Mud Emperor Pavilion. This unworthy one engraved a Mud Emperor Pavilion seal and presented it to him, and also signed the board in his pavilion. (Qu Que)

A Record of Ink Farming 171

— Lu Yucen

The painter Wang Shizi recently moved to No. 9 Maigali Road, Disiwei Road. A small two-story building, bright, clean, and quiet. He splashes ink from morning to night, and his paintings become more outstanding and elegant. I once commented that Shizi's paintings are light but have spirit, beautiful but not vulgar, which friends thought was an apt description. The other day, Shizi asked me to write a plaque inscription, "Ink Farming Cottage." When asked about its meaning, it was simply a homophone of Maigali. So I jokingly wrote a record for it: Shizi recently rented a house in Maigali, north of Shanghai, and named his hall "Ink Farming Cottage," a homophone. Pens and inks can be used as farming tools, and I am fortunate to still have my tongue. Rice farming has descendants who will pass it on without fail. You are enjoying great fame for your artistic achievements and celebrating a bountiful harvest. The joy of his solitary pleasures is something that even the so-called ten thousand bushels of grain and a thousand chariots of horses in the world cannot add to. Maigali and Ink Farming are the best. I put down my pen and wrote this record, also a play on words. Now I write it to show those who know Shizi.

Northern Tour Images and Others (5) 172

— Yao Sufeng

Self-narration by Movie Star Hu Die

Later, in Beiping, "Fate in Tears and Laughter" began filming. Because the location shots in the film had to be realistic, it was decided to go to Beiping to shoot them. Beiping is a place I used to visit! I seem to still remember those towering palaces, the ancient city walls, the tourists in Central Park, the beautiful rickshaws on the road, the dry weather, the strong sunlight, and even the crisp voices and straightforward attitude of the people of Beiping... everything, everything, although it has been many years since I have been there, I have never forgotten it. Therefore, when the news of the departure to Beiping was announced in the company, many people were as happy as I was. Before the departure, I told many people who had never been to Beiping about the scenery of Beiping, almost making Beiping a paradise for us. The most interesting thing was that I told them that in Beiping, you could rent a large house for twenty silver dollars, which surprised friends who lived in small rooms in Shanghai. I told them that you would never see heavy rain in Beiping all year round, but Mr. Cheng Bugao regretfully took out the newly purchased raincoat from his suitcase.

Walking in the middle of a group of people with infinite interest and infinite hope, I was especially proud. At this time, everyone had woken up from the busy preparations and said goodbye to our photography studio with an expression that seemed to carry some due courtesy, but there was no feeling of parting. Several cars carried a group of people who were like laughing children. From this moment on, we seemed to be in another world.

From Shanghai North Station to Jinan, our group was constantly watched by others. "This is the Star Film Company going to Beiping to shoot Fate in Tears and Laughter." "This is Hu Die,"... "This is Zheng Xiaoqiu"... "This is..." became many words familiar to our ears; "Watched by ten eyes and pointed at by ten fingers," we seemed to be subjected to even more serious surveillance. On the train, we read newspapers, talked, and didn't feel tired from the long journey. I can't tell you all the trivial things during the journey. I only remember that when we arrived in Jinan, many reporters came to visit us on the train. Mr. Zhang Shichuan smiled and said to us, "It's a great honor! This is the treatment for important people."

Record of Two Buildings in Military Life (19) 173

— Master of Qiuxingfu Studio

Chapter 3: Yu and Liang Arrive Together, Causing the Feast to Disperse; Yin and Xing Avoid Each Other, No One Knows Who Lost the Jewel Box

Liang Xiaoyun suddenly became slightly angry and said, "If you have friends coming, just let them come. With me sitting here, what does it matter? Am I not your friend? Even though I am a woman, does that mean girlfriends can't openly come and sit here? Do I have to sneak around, hide, and avoid seeing other people's faces? How strange. You actually dislike me now. I want to ask you, what kind of person do you take me for? And what are your intentions? "An Yutian didn't mean to say anything wrong, but got a nose full of ash for nothing. He was also severely scolded by her. He felt a wave of injustice in his heart, and sweat beads as big as soybeans dripped down his forehead. He wiped it with a handkerchief and tried to defend himself with a bitter smile, "No, it's really an old senior coming. Also, an antique from the 17th or 18th century. Stubborn and doesn't approve of free interaction between men and women. In case he acts old-fashioned and says something unpleasant when he sees you, wouldn't that make everyone unhappy and just make you angry? That's why I thought of asking you not to meet this kind of person to avoid some unnecessary troubles. But I didn't expect you to be so suspicious and say such angry words. I'm so wronged." As he spoke, he almost choked and was about to cry. Seeing him so distressed and pitiful, Liang Xiaoyun's heart suddenly softened, and she relaxed her tone and said, "Since you said that, is it true that some old, stubborn country bumpkin is coming? I don't want to get angry with this kind of person either. Naturally, it's better to leave first. But why didn't you explain it clearly earlier and make me feel uncomfortable? Never mind. Considering that you haven't been in a good mood these past two days and your mind is confused, I won't argue with you. I'm leaving now. But you must come to my place tomorrow. Don't break your promise. Otherwise, I don't care what new or old antiques you have in your house. I'm still going to come and find you myself." Seeing that she had dispelled her doubts and was willing to leave, An Yutian felt a heavy weight lifted from his heart. He secretly chanted "Amitabha." But thinking that time was pressing, the sooner she left, the better. He stood up from the table and said, "I'm full. If you don't want to eat anymore, I'll call a car for you." Liang Xiaoyun smiled, "What's the rush? Are you urging me to leave? I hate being pushed around the most. If you rush me, I'll get angry again. Although I've had enough wine and food, I can't just run out with my mouth covered in grease. I need to wash my face. Please, ask the waiter to bring me a basin of hot water."

Financial and Gold Markets Continue to Decline 174

Unpredictable Changes. Yesterday, the price of gold continued to fall, with further declines. The changes remained intense. There were twelve taels of returns in the morning and afternoon, making it unpredictable. Peers were at a loss. Finally, it fell by about four taels again. It opened slightly lower. Although overseas silver markets rose, U.S. silver was in short supply, so there was no significant impact. Due to the unsettled situation, large investors vigorously sold. Exchange rates for British currency, etc., tended to loosen and were listed longer by one grade. As a result, market conditions turned weak, and there was a rush to the lower reaches. There were frequent declines of more than ten taels, almost falling to 660 taels. However, because the U.S. exchange rate was still stable, it was due to small exchange rate adjustments. In particular, buyers also revived and calmly went upwards, resulting in around seventy taels. There were no major overseas news. In the afternoon, because it was Saturday and the market was closed, it was said that the swap rate was raised to three taels, which was posted by the bulls, but there was no transaction. It was also found that there were quite a few chaotic moments in the market this week. It was very sharp at the beginning of the week, but then became sluggish. The maximum price was 99 taels, and the minimum price was 61 taels, a difference of 38 taels. Overall, compared to the previous Saturday, it fell 9 taels and 6 qian, etc.

It opened down one tael. At the opening, it was slightly lower by one tael, counted as 672 taels. The large strip rose again by 8 fen 3. The forward price was 5/16. The silver price only rose by 1/4. It immediately returned up 1 tael and a half, to 73 taels and a half. Suddenly, Hengxing, Hengchangyong, Yuanheng, Wanxing, Shunli, etc., sold off one after another, really because the atmosphere was bad. The supply in the market was greater than demand, so the price plummeted by 11 taels. Only counted as one or two taels of the head, at 9:15, it was 62 taels and a half. Later, because a telegram came from India to buy British gold at 11 pence to 10 pence 9375, sold by Mitsui, and because Yuanmaoyong, Dadecheng, Tongdachang, etc., all entered, Hengxing also suddenly bought three taels and zero, for 65 taels and 8 qian. When the announcement of British gold was released, it was extended by 25, and the U.S. dollar was also increased by 25, and then it retreated to 63 taels and a half. It was almost that the far-month U.S. dollar was absorbed by brokers, 33 yuan, 1875. In an instant, retail households bought in, adding three taels, but the U.S. dollar could be settled at three yuan, and because Qianchangxiang, Dadecheng, etc., tended to sell, and there were few buyers, the price fell by one to five taels and zero.

Approaching 60 taels, at 9:30, it was 61 taels. Soon after, Anda absorbed the May U.S. dollar at 33 yuan 125, and the April British gold did 10 pence 9375. At this time, the sellers stopped slightly, and Xiexingyong, Yuanmaoyong, Hengxing, Yifengyong, etc., went to the market to buy, so the price gradually rose. After 10:30, it was 67 taels and 8 qian, but for a moment there were two taels of ups and downs. Later, because Tong Taichang sold, and HSBC issued the May U.S. dollar at three yuan, it immediately suppressed it by three taels, to 64 taels and 8 qian. After 10:45, there were often more than two taels of ups and downs. After 11:00, Dadecheng, Hengxing, Shunli, Wanxing, etc., competed to buy, and Muggary absorbed the April U.S. dollar at 32 yuan 9375, so the price increased by more than three taels. At 11:15, it was 68 taels and 3 qian. After only three minutes, it fell to 6 taels and 7 qian. Buyers rose up again, and before long, Fuyu, Hongkangyong, Yuhe, Hengxing, Daxingyong, Yuanmaoyong, Yifengyong, etc., all came to compete to buy, but the number was not huge. Generally, hat snatchers on the platform worked hard to hype it up, until 11:45, it was 70 taels, but it was a flash in the pan, and it went back in.

Seventy taels, it was 68 taels and 8 qian. By the time the market closed at noon, it was 69 taels and 2 qian. Generally, retail households were eager to sell, not to carry it overnight, and because it was a Saturday market close, the price fell by more than two taels again, only about 67 taels. It continued to fall three taels and eight. Compared to the previous day's listing, it fell three taels and eight qian. (Falling for three consecutive days totaled 23 taels and 4 qian.) Slight Signs of Weakness in the Cotton Market 180

The cotton market situation is calm. Due to the decline in gold prices, and especially the weakness in the American cotton market, with most expecting Indian cotton prices to fall, the market trend is weakening. However, recently, actual demand has picked up somewhat, and selling prices are also high. Due to a lack of supply from various sources, the Hankou and Ningbo trading houses are observing the high prices with very ambitious sentiments.

This month, Hankou standard longs have been liquidating. The Hankou standard front-month futures market opened at the exchange with minimal over-the-counter trading of American cotton. The current month rose five points, and the distant month fell five points. In the afternoon, the current month's longs liquidated, falling 1.5 cents. Total daily trading volume was 44,600 bales. Sales included 1,900 bales of Jifeng, 1,400 bales of Yuda, 1,700 bales of Changhe, 1,500 bales of Daji, and 2,200 bales of Changfeng. Purchases included 1,000 bales of Hengyi, 1,300 bales of Dafu, 2,200 bales of Shenchang, and 1,500 bales of Yifeng. The Hankou standard closing prices are listed below:

Grain and Rice Market in He Xia Turns Stable 183

Yesterday, the supply in Hu Nan was not abundant, and the inventory in Pu was weak. Although demand from urban and rural shops was flat, due to monetary conditions, the Suzhou and Tongxiang merchants offered slightly lower prices. The supply of thin early rice was sporadic and very limited. Trading on this street was extremely quiet. The market was high, stable, and slightly weak by one cent. Demand for Lu Yang pointed rice was scarce, and the situation appeared weak. General goods for sale were unchanged.

The supply on Xin Zha West Road came from over thirty firms. Trading on this street was not brisk. Changshu and Xixi Northern japonica rice was priced at the top end, and secondary rice was slightly weak by one cent. Early and late rice sales were very active, and the situation appeared favorable. Trading in Du Du pointed rice was unfavorable, and opening prices were reduced by several cents. Exchange rates remained unchanged.

Imported Rice Will Likely Rebound After Weakness 184

Foreign Firms Cover Short Positions Quietly

Taizhou Rice Continues to Arrive

Yesterday, the imported rice market saw little buying and selling. Only one transaction was reported in the general market in the morning: 400 bags of Saigon rice at $11.75 and 200 bags of Xiaojiao rice at $10.01. Prices were up 6-7 cents to 1 cent compared to the previous market. No transactions occurred in the afternoon because sellers were unwilling to sell. However, foreign firms and importers engaged in new transactions and sold recovered goods. It is said that some foreign merchants are searching the market to buy futures contracts to cover previously sold positions because it is rumored that Japanese merchants are expanding their purchases in the producing areas, and the spot goods have been completely bought up. Foreign firms previously sold a significant amount to the market, and it is feared that they will not be able to deliver the actual goods as contracted. If this rumor is confirmed, the market will experience a significant rebound. Yesterday, the price of recovered goods on this street increased by 3-5 cents, resulting in no transactions. However, Taizhou rice continued to arrive in large quantities in recent days. Another batch arrived yesterday, with 400 bags of Taizhou white rice offered at $11.65 to $11.57, 500 bags of early rice at $10.025, and 300 bags of brown rice at $10.06, all of which were higher than the previous prices.

The Flour Market is Weak but Stable 185

Yesterday, the flour market generally showed signs of being flat and weak. Because the quotation for foreign wheat was still down by 1-2 cents, manufacturers have already made firm orders for foreign wheat, so their attitude is naturally unfavorable. In addition, as the end of the current month approaches, some of the head-covering warehouse warrants from before the New Year have been returned due to the quality of the goods. Therefore, February is showing stability due to head-covering and the standard for customer purchases. For distant months, factories are slightly selling, and the overall situation is flat. As a result, the current month fell 7.5 cents compared to the previous day, February was up 2.5 cents, March was unchanged, April was down 2.5 cents, and May and June were down 7.5 cents.

The Wheat Market Lags 186

It's Not Easy to Get Better

Yesterday, the wheat futures market generally showed signs of hovering. As the current month's delivery approached, it initially remained sluggish, down 3-5 cents from the previous day. Later, it recovered as manufacturers were rumored to have buying intentions. The various distant months also showed weakness in the morning sessions, but in the afternoon sessions, as market sentiment stabilized slightly, there was a slight recovery. It is observed that it is not easy to get better. As a result, the current month was unchanged from the previous day, February was down 2 cents, March was down 1 cent, April was unchanged, May was up 1 cent, and there was no comparison for June.

Standard Prices of Piece Goods, Wool Fabrics Also Fell Sharply 187

Imported Goods Were Originally Cheaper... Market Sales Have Reached the Season's End

The wool and wool fabric market is currently in the off-season. Selling prices have been weakening every day since last month, and standards have not yet fallen, although they have long been secretly reduced. However, well-known and established brands in the wool fabric business, such as Rongtai's 15330 yuan Zhigong, Deki's 1440 and Anli's Jubaopen, Lulin, Deki's Fengshenbang Walter Cloth, Deki's 1339 assorted bilges, and other goods, are generally considered indicators of price movement in the wool fabric market. Therefore, the rise and fall of the above goods serve as benchmarks for other wool fabrics. Unexpectedly, the market prices of these goods also fell sharply the day before yesterday, with an average drop of several cents per yard. For example, Rongtai's 15330 yuan Zhigong woolen cloth was reduced to 7 liang 7 qian 5 fen, Deki's 1440 Walter Cloth was 5 liang 1 qian 5 fen, Anli's Jubaopen was 7 liang, Deki's 1339 assorted bilges was 3 liang 2 qian 2 fen 5 li, and Fengshenbang Walter Cloth was 4 liang 3 qian 5 fen. The reason for the sharp decline is the direct impact of cheaper imported goods and stagnant market sales.

Silk and Tea Foreign Firms Silk Market Lifeless 189

Due to the slight drop in Japanese silk prices, overseas Shanghai white filature factories reported that silk prices were 300-400 taels lower than the cost of the factory silk, resulting in excessive losses. The market atmosphere was dull. Yesterday, only Taihe imported 5 bales of Baigan silk and Gaobei imported 10 bales of yellow coarse silk. Prices remained flat and weak.

There are Still Over a Thousand Bales of Chefoo Raw Silk Inventory 190

Chefoo raw silk produced in Zhejiang and Hubei is widely sold in Europe and America. Since the new silk was launched last autumn, sales in Europe have been difficult to achieve smoothly, but the market has been able to maintain its position. This is because the markets in New York and Lyon have been affected by the low price of Japanese silk. Moreover, due to the intense Anglo-Indian political struggle, the export of Chefoo raw silk has become even more difficult. The inventory in Shanghai warehouses is not weak. The total inventory of Chefoo raw silk in the city is still over 1,500 bales, of which fancy-cart dry silk accounts for 70%, and the rest is flat-cart large silk.

Premium Eyebrow Tea Exports are Brisk 191

Yesterday, foreign tea firms in this port, especially those dealing in high-end Zhenmei tea such as Lüzhuang, Xiehe, and Tianxiang, continued their efforts to purchase tea. Medium-grade and ordinary Zhenmei teas were also being actively traded by firms such as Yihe and Tongfu. Trading was unusually brisk, with total sales in the city reaching over 1,100 chests. Selling prices were all trending firmer. The current inventory of green tea from Lüzhuang is becoming increasingly scarce, and the sales of native tea are also showing signs of activity.

Hardware, Pig Lead Sales are Uniquely Brisk 192

Recently, the hardware market has shown signs of nearing an end, so there are very few goods in the market that are showing any vitality. However, the pig lead market, which has been stagnant for a long time, has reversed from weak to strong. The price is 14 taels 1 qian 5 fen per dan, which is 1 qian 5 fen higher than before. Although yesterday was Saturday, there were still over 2,000 dan traded. As a result, the market goods suddenly became scarce after being purchased, and the sentiment is very good. There is great hope that the market will continue to improve.

Coal, Anthracite Sales are Sluggish 193

Small Forum

Fortunately, Advertising Literature 195

"The ancients always loved swords. A three-foot Qingping sword emerges under the candlelight. Seeing the country's deep-seated hatred, they all relied on it to avenge it. Now the sword has become a weapon of the past, and China's armament is difficult to compare with the world, causing heroes and patriots to sigh in vain. Sitting alone late at night, resentment is like a mountain. Only by smoking ×× cigarettes can one slightly alleviate the frustration..."

Such "advertising literature" has been popular in Shanghai for a while and has long been "commonplace," so there is no need to criticize it.

"Smoking ×× brand cigarettes" is enough to show "not forgetting patriotism." This logic is a characteristic of Shanghai's advertising literature. By analogy, "Yunnan-Guizhou-Sichuan native opium" is also still showing "not forgetting patriotism." "Playing mahjong" and "gambling on pai gow" are also "not forgetting patriotism" because Yunnan-Guizhou-Sichuan native products are the best among domestic goods, and mahjong and pai gow are also the best among domestic goods, so they are still "not forgetting patriotism."

Moreover, there are many ways to be patriotic: "love without forgetting to save the country," "reading without forgetting to save the country," "being an official without forgetting to be patriotic," and even "whoring without forgetting to save the country." These theories are all very logical and are absolutely true.

However, when the Japanese rioted in the Hongkou North Sichuan Road area, burned the Sanyou Industrial Society, and destroyed Chinese stores, our national salvation groups, suicide squads, and volunteer armies were still holding meetings, giving speeches, posting slogans, and issuing circular telegrams. In fact, those who earnestly do national salvation work in writing, on paper, and orally are not only profit-seeking merchants, speculative politicians, and frivolous young people, but also the great men of our country.

Each great man's declaration, circular telegram, plan, and outline is full of "not forgetting patriotism," but in reality, they are all selling plaster, which does not deviate from the principle of "smoking ×× brand cigarettes and still not forgetting patriotism."

Advertising is popular, and the country will perish without a day. Alas!

Popular Literature

An Open Letter Yun Zhong 196

Qiong Mei:

Since this weak motherland has been invaded by the Japanese bandits, how turbulent and painful are my surging hot blood and this fragile soul! Therefore, at this time, I only feel that the entire universe is extremely dark and the entire life is extremely restless. Finally, I feel that the air of grief and indignation has stirred my heart, and I am determined to fulfill my small responsibilities.

Because of the rushing of hot blood, the stimulation of sadness, and... ah! My weak nerves have been striving to awaken me, occupying my entire soul, and inspiring my will, so I naturally completely accepted it. However, my heart has enjoyed the invigorating medicine, and I really feel more cheerful! Therefore, the brain filled with excitement has instructed me to join this large team that automatically goes to the Northeast to swear to resist Japan.

But our goal of fighting to the death has easily achieved a satisfactory result. Finally, we are going to the front line to work hard to complete our task of killing the enemy! In that moment of gunfire, countless ferocious enemies flashed into our eyes. At this time, ah! My jealous heart has been aroused, and I can't wait to immediately use my boiling hot blood and this fearless spirit to sweep away this monstrous evil spirit and wash away our greatest shame. But the sound of advancing has risen, how happy are we? So, the flying-like healthy feet are also showing their power, rushing to the enemy's front line, and my god gun that kills the enemy is firing bursts of hot bullets, finally flying into the enemy's vital points, and the enemy's front line is completely shaken. Finally, we occupied the enemy's entire defense and won the greatest victory. Qiong Mei! When this news reaches your ears, I think you will be very happy, right?

Now we are going to meet this barbaric enemy again with the spirit of courage and perseverance, but the loud call has also sounded! Ah! I, Qiong, who urgently need to pack my bags and set off, have to put down my pen temporarily. Qiong Mei! Goodbye! I wish you

Effort! Yours, Min Ge, respectfully wrote, month, day

Popular Science

Egg Suspended in Water Su Su 197

This is an interesting physics trick that everyone can try. It costs very little and yields an important principle in physics.

Now, prepare the necessary items: a fresh egg, a tall glass bottle filled with water, and a packet of salt.

First, put the egg into the bottle. The egg is heavier than water and naturally sinks to the bottom of the bottle. Now, slowly add salt to the water, a little at a time, while stirring the water. When the salt is added to the appropriate amount, the egg will completely obey your command. You lift it up and place it in the center of the bottle. As soon as you take your hand away, it will still stop moving. If you raise it a little higher or lower it a little, it will also obey your orders and dare not move around on its own.

The principle of this phenomenon is quite simple. Because the specific gravity of the egg is greater than that of clean water, the egg sinks. Adding salt to the water turns the clean water into salt water. The specific gravity of salt water is greater than that of clean water. The more salt that is added, the greater the specific gravity. When the specific gravity of the salt water is equal to the specific gravity of the egg, the egg will neither float nor sink and will stop in the water. If you add more salt so that the specific gravity of the salt water is greater than that of the egg, the egg will float on the surface of the water.

At the same time, there is a ridiculous fact that comes to mind that is the same principle as this experiment. It may be worth mentioning in passing. Everyone knows that to the east of the city of Jerusalem is a saltwater lake called the Dead Sea. The water there contains 25% salt, and the specific gravity is particularly high. No matter who runs to that place, they can swim very safely.

Street Sociology

The Call of the City Xue De 198

People who have never been to the metropolis of Shanghai always have fantasies of a "great, mysterious, and enchanting gold mine." But as soon as you step into the metropolis of Shanghai, you feel that it hides sadness, depravity, pain... and constant calls!

In the morning, lying in bed, you hear:

"Little cabbage, green vegetables, radishes!..." This voice is always sad and poignant, and it will give you a feeling of sadness. After a while, another burst follows: "Shen Bao, Shi Bao... Xinwen Bao!..." a rough voice

At noon, the sounds gradually become more complex, sad, heavy, light, sandy, broken, and rumbling in the streets and alleys. That kind of life's cry makes it impossible for your brain to rest for a moment. Even if you walk in the street, the ragged children and the sick and declining old paupers will follow behind you.

"Sir, young master... do something good!..." a burst of chaotic cries. Is it a little more peaceful in the evening? It's really more peaceful! But soon, that kind of call will strike your heart again in the quiet night and the secluded alley:

"Olives, buy one for a cent... sandalwood olives... buy olives!..."

This voice is always clear and melodious, more natural and wonderful than any music! But its ending is too sad and too sour! I can't bear to listen any longer!

Soon you hear:

The hissing sound of a cracked bamboo shell, followed by: "Fire bamboo, be careful!..." a short, abrupt, sandy voice gradually approaching from afar, gradually receding from near...

Late at night, I am awakened by a troubled battle. I barely hear:

"Ham dumplings!..."

"Sweet osmanthus white sugar lotus seed porridge, taro with sugar!..." I have lived in Shanghai for ten years, and every day I wake up sadly, sleep sadly, and have to be startled sadly in the middle of the night!

"The call of the city, the call of the city!..." When will you disappear from my ears?

From All Directions

Talking About Students' Three-G Principles Meng Ping 199

Since the Industrial Revolution in the 18th century, everything in society has been built on capitalism. Modern schools have also followed the trend of capitalization. Poor students are unable to enter, and even those with some assets can barely study in school, but whether they will have the opportunity to serve after graduation is another problem. Therefore, during their studies, the magic power of money invades their minds. Goldism naturally arises.

Under the teachings of Confucianism in China, interactions between men and women are subject to great oppression. The idea of "men and women not giving or receiving things hand-to-hand" advocates "the orders of parents and the words of matchmakers" to determine the lifelong affairs of men and women. Modern students, influenced by new ideas, have been instilled with ideas such as open social interactions and free marriage. The old etiquette of the past must be fundamentally overturned in the hope of obtaining a happy marriage and enjoying the gentle blessings of beauty. Girls have become their target.

We often hear that some people cannot take the opportunity to apply to schools because they do not have a diploma. Even if they have a very good level, they cannot obtain the understanding of the school authorities. Therefore, most people value qualifications, such as when a university professor comes to teach, the first concept for students is whether he has studied abroad. How is his knowledge is secondary. This emphasis on qualifications rather than level of achievement is indeed forced on them by the system of society. Gradism has been created.

Some people say that students' three-G principles are a manifestation of educational bankruptcy. I am not judging whether what they say is correct. I am only pointing out the reason for its occurrence.

Classroom Sketch Meng Ping 200

When the students heard that there was a female teacher coming to teach political science today, everyone felt a kind of joy in their hearts and felt that this was something worth celebrating. School A, which had never hired a female teacher before, suddenly heard that there was a female teacher coming to teach us today, so naturally, a feeling of joy arose. Thinking of the male teacher's coarse voice, ugly face, and serious attitude, they hoped that time would pass sooner and waited for the political science course to arrive.

The bell rang with a clang. The director of academic affairs accompanied the female teacher into the classroom. The students held their breath and listened to the director's introductory remarks, saying that this female teacher was a graduate of a certain university, had novel ideas, and was knowledgeable. After the director left, she began to teach. When she asked the students if they had any questions, student Li stood up and asked:

"How many political parties are there in the United States? Teacher!" asked student Li.

"Two political parties," she answered.

"Which two political parties?"

"Two political parties."

"Which party is Hoover in?"

"Um... I'll talk about it next time!"

After saying the above sentence, she left with her books.

Shanghai Story

Shanghai Story (18) Compiled and Translated by Zhou Rong 201

The Anglo-American troop deployment having been decided, they marched to Garden Lane (now Nanjing Road) at 3:30 PM that afternoon, raising flags and beating drums. From there, they advanced further to the area between today's Nanjing Road and Zhejiang Road (formerly the eastern boundary of the racecourse) and stopped, awaiting the actions of the Qing government forces. Seeing that the government forces made no move, the Anglo-American allied forces estimated that it might not be possible to defeat more than two thousand people with three hundred and eighty men. They immediately felt disheartened, but since the troops had already been dispatched, they were unwilling to retreat and show weakness. They then divided their troops into two teams. The American troops attacked the front of the government forces from the left side of the racecourse, and the British troops advanced straight forward to attack the side of the government forces.

According to the eyewitness account of W.S. Wetmore, who accompanied the American troops, the American troops deployed two cannons between the graveyards, no more than two or three hundred yards from the Qing camp. At 4:00 PM, they opened fire as a signal to start the attack. The British troops also attacked at the same time. Suddenly, countless red dots moved extremely fast in the desolate grass of the mounds. These were the members of the Small Swords Society in the city who came out to help the foreigners attack the government troops. From this, it can be seen that the foreigners had agreed with the Small Swords Society in advance, so they dared to attack more than two thousand people with more than three hundred men. As the number of Red Turbans increased, the government troops' camp wavered and began to retreat.

The American commander, Skeli, took advantage of the situation to order a charge. Unexpectedly, they were blocked by a mud ditch. The ditch was fifteen to twenty feet wide and about four feet deep with water. It was the outer moat of the Qing camp. Inside the moat was a high wall six or seven feet high. The American troops were blocked by the government troops' artillery fire at this point and retreated to the cemetery. The American military action ended there. The moat that stopped the American troops' advance was called Zhoujiajingbang, which was incorporated into the boundary of Nichengbang many years later.

As for the British troops, they advanced straight ahead and encountered a bridge in front of Zhoujingbang. They then changed their course to the left and attacked the first barrack. Because there were cannons placed in front of the barrack, the British troops suffered few casualties. However, the deputy captain, Du, first entered the camp. The government troops had no intention of fighting for long, so they set fire to the barrack and left, retreating to the south of the county town.

The reasons for the government troops' retreat were: first, the Small Swords Society came out of the city to help the foreign troops; and second, they feared that starting a diplomatic incident would cause a major disaster. Moreover, the lack of military knowledge of Gilhangke and his inability to respond well were also reasons for the failure.

In this battle, the Anglo-American allied forces suffered two dead and fifteen wounded, two of whom later died from their injuries. The government troops also suffered no more than fifty dead and wounded. This is what is called the "Battle of Nicheng."

French Troops Assist Government Troops in Attacking the City

At that time, the county town was still occupied by the Small Swords Society. The obvious fact was that the government was concerned about cutting off aid from the concession. French Naval Commander Laguerre believed that the reason why the bandits in the city were resisting so stubbornly was because the British were secretly providing them with aid and blamed the British for not being able to strictly maintain neutrality.
